As part of this, firms should put in place appropriate and risk-sensitive policies and procedures to ensure that their approach to applying CDD measures does not result in unduly denying legitimate customers access to financial services., Where a customer has legitimate and credible reasons for being unable to provide traditional forms of identity documentation, firms should consider mitigating ML/TF risk in other ways, including by

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93658: a) Adjusting the level and intensity of monitoring in a way that is commensurate to the ML/TF risk associated with the customer, including the risk that a customer who may have provided a weaker form of identity documentation may not be who they claim to be; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93659: b) Offering only basic financial products and services, which restrict the ability of users to abuse these products and services for financial crime purposes. Such basic products and services may also make it easier for firms to identify unusual transactions or patterns of transactions, including the unintended use of the product; but it is important that any limits be proportionate and do not unreasonably or unnecessarily limit customers' access to financial products and services.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93660: 4.11. Firms may wish to refer to the EBA's Opinion on the application of customer due diligence measures to customers who are asylum seekers from higher-risk third countries or territories (EBA-OP-2016-07).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93661: Beneficial owners

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93662: 4.12. When discharging their obligations set out in Article 13(1)(b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 to understand the customer's ownership and control structure firms should take at least the followings steps :

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93663: a) Firms should ask the customer who their beneficial owners are;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93664: b) Firms should document the information obtained.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93665: c) Firms should then take all necessary and reasonable measures to verify the information: to achieve this, firms should consider using beneficial ownership registers where available.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93666: d) Steps b) and c) should be applied on a risk-sensitive basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_93667: Beneficial ownership registers

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93669: 4.13. Firms should be mindful that using information contained in beneficial ownership registers does not, in itself, fulfil their duty to take adequate and risk-sensitive measures to identity the beneficial owner and verify their identity. Firms may have to take additional steps to identify and verify the beneficial owner, in particular where the risk associated with the business relationship is increased or where the firm has doubts that the person listed in the register is the ultimate beneficial owner.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93670: Control through other means

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93671: 4.14. The requirement to identify, and take all necessary and reasonable measures to verify the identity of the beneficial owner relates only to the natural person who ultimately owns or controls the customer. However, to comply with their obligations under Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should also take reasonable measures to understand the customer's ownership and control structure.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93672: 4.15. The measures firms take to understand the customer's ownership and control structure should be sufficient so that the firm can be reasonably satisfied that it understands the risk associated with different layers of ownership and control. In particular, firms should be satisfied that,

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93673: a) the customer's ownership and control structure is not unduly complex or opaque; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93674: b) complex or opaque ownership and control structures have a legitimate legal or economic reason.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93675: 4.16. To meet their obligations under Article 33 (1) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should report to the FIU if the customer's ownership and control structure give rise to suspicion and they have reasonable grounds to suspect that the funds may be the proceeds of criminal activity or are related to terrorist financing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93676: 4.17. Firms should pay particular attention to persons who may exercise 'control through other means' under Article 3(6) (a)(i) of Directive (EU) 2015/849. Examples of 'control through other means' firms should consider include, but are not limited to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93677: a) control without direct ownership, for example through close family relationships, or historical or contractual associations;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93678: b) using, enjoying or benefiting from the assets owned by the customer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93679: c) responsibility for strategic decisions that fundamentally affect the business practices or general direction of a legal person.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:28]
PARAGRAPH_93680: 4.18. Firms should decide, on a risk-sensitive basis, whether to verify the customer's ownership and control structure.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93682: Identifying the customer's senior managing officials

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93683: 4.19. Where the customer is a legal entity, firms should make every effort to identify the beneficial owner as defined in Article 3(6)(a) (i) of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93684: 4.20. Firms should resort to identifying the customer's senior managing officials as beneficial owners only if:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93685: a) They have exhausted all possible means of identifying the natural person who ultimately owns or controls the customer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93686: b) Their inability to identify the natural person who ultimately owns or controls the customer does not give rise to suspicions of ML/TF; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93687: c) They are satisfied that the reason given by the customer as to why the natural person who ultimately owns or controls the customer cannot be identified is plausible.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93688: 4.21. When deciding which senior managing official, or which senior managing officials, to identify as beneficial owner, firms should consider who has ultimate and overall responsibility for the customer and takes binding decisions on the customer's behalf.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93689: 4.22. In those cases, firms should clearly document their reasons for identifying the senior manager, rather than the customer's beneficial owner, and must keep records of their actions7.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93690: Identifying the beneficial owner of a public administration or a state-owned enterprises

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93691: 4.23. Where the customer is a public administration or a state-owned enterprise, firms should follow the guidance in guidelines 4.21 and 4.22 to identify the senior managing official.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93692: 4.24. In those cases, and in particular where the risk associated with the relationship is increased, for example because the state-owned enterprise is from a country associated with high levels of corruption, firms should take risk-sensitive steps to establish that the person they have identified as the beneficial owner is properly authorised by the customer to act on the customer's behalf.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93693: 4.25. Firms should also have due regard to the possibility that the senior managing official of the customer may be a PEP. Should this be the case, firms must apply EDD measures to that senior managing official in line with Article 18 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, and assess whether the extent to which the PEP can influence the customer gives rise to increased ML/TF risk and whether it may be necessary to apply EDD measures to the customer.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:29]
PARAGRAPH_93694: 7 Article 3(6)(a)(ii) of Directive (EU) 2015/849

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93696: Evidence of identity

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93697: 4.26. To comply with their obligations under Article 13(1)(a) and (b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should verify their customer's identity and, where applicable, beneficial owners' identity, on the basis of reliable and independent information and data, whether this is obtained remotely, electronically or in documentary form.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93698: 4.27. Firms should set out in their policies and procedures which information and data they will treat as reliable and independent for CDD purposes. As part of this, firms should consider

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93699: a) What makes data or information reliable. Firms should consider different degrees of reliability, which they should determine based on

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93700: i. the extent to which the customer had to undergo certain checks to obtain the information or data provided;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93701: ii. the official status, if any, of the person or institution that carried out those checks;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93702: iii. the level of assurance associated with any digital ID system used; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93703: iv. the ease with which the identity information or data provided can be forged.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93704: b) What makes data or information independent. Firms should consider different degrees of independence, which they should determine based on the extent to which the person or institution that originally issued or provided the data or information:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93705: i. is linked to the customer through direct personal, professional or family ties; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93706: ii. could have been unduly influenced by the customer.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93707: In most cases, firms should be able to treat government-issued information or data as providing the highest level of independence and reliability.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93708: 4.28. Firms should assess the risks associated with each type of evidence provided and the method of identification and verification used and ensure that the method and type chosen is commensurate with the ML/TF risk associated with the customer.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93709: Non-face to face situations

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93710: 4.29. To perform their obligations under Article 13(1) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, where the business relationship is initiated, established, or conducted in non-face to face situations or an occasional transaction is done in non-face to face situations, firms should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:30]
PARAGRAPH_93711: a) take adequate measures to be satisfied that the customer is who he claims to be; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93713: b) assess whether the non-face to face nature of the relationship or occasional transaction gives rise to increased ML/TF risk and if so, adjust their CDD measures accordingly. When assessing the risk associated with non-face to face relationships, firms should have regard to the risk factors set out in Guideline 2.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93714: 4.30. Where the risk associated with a non-face to face relationship or an occasional transaction is increased, firms should apply EDD measures in line with Guidelines 4.46. Firms should consider in particular whether enhanced measures to verify the identity of the customer or enhanced ongoing monitoring of the relationship would be appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93715: 4.31. Firms should have regard to the fact that the use of electronic means of identification does not of itself give rise to increased ML/TF risk, in particular where these electronic means provide a high level of assurance under Regulation (EU) 910/2014.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93716: Using innovative technological means to verify identity

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93717: 4.32. Directive (EU) 2015/849 is technology neutral and firms may choose to use electronic or documentary means, or a combination thereof, to evidence their customers' identity; but pursuant to Article 13(1)(a) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 firms should make sure that this evidence is based on data or information from reliable and independent sources.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93718: 4.33. Firms that use or intend to use innovative technological means for identification and verification purposes should assess the extent to which the use of innovative technological solutions can address, or might exacerbate, the ML/TF risks, in particular in non-face to face situations. As part of their assessment, firms should have a clear view on:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93719: a) ICT and security risks, in particular the risk that the innovative solution may be unsuitable or unreliable or could be tampered with;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93720: b) qualitative risks, in particular the risk that the sources of information used for verification purposes are not sufficiently independent and reliable and therefore fall short of Union law or national law; and the risk that the extent of identity verification provided by the innovative solution is not commensurate with the level of ML/TF risk associated with the business relationship;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93721: c) legal risks, in particular the risk that the technological solution provider does not comply with applicable data protection legislation; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93722: d) impersonation fraud risks, that is, the risk that a customer is not who they claim to be. Firms should also consider the risk that the person is not a real person.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:31]
PARAGRAPH_93723: 4.34. Firms that use an external provider, rather than develop their own innovative solution in- house, remain ultimately responsible for meeting their CDD obligations. They should be clear about their relationship with the innovative solution provider (e.g. whether it is an

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93725: outsourcing relationship, or whether the use of the innovative solution constitutes a form of reliance on a third party as per Section 4 of Directive (EU) 2015/849), and take sufficient steps to be satisfied that the innovative solution provider:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93726: a) is registered with relevant national authorities to access and store personal data to EU legal standards in compliance with Regulation (EU) 2016/679 (General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)8 and legislation by which the GDPR has been implemented;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93727: b) accesses and uses a sufficient range of data from different sources and across time, having regard to the following elements in particular

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93728: i. electronic evidence based on a customer's passport is unlikely to be sufficient in a non-face to face context without accompanying checks to ensure that the customer is who they say they are, and that the document has not been tampered with; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93729: ii. a single data source or a single point in time is unlikely to be enough to meet verification standards in most situations

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93730: c) is contractually bound to comply with duties required by their agreement and binding norms of Union Law and national law, and to inform the firm immediately should anything change; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93731: d) operates transparently, so that the firm knows at all times which checks were carried out, which sources were used, what the results were and how robust these results were.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93732: 4.35. Where the external provider is a firm established in a third country, the firm should ensure that it understands the legal risks and operational risks and data protection requirements associated therewith and mitigates those risks effectively.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93733: 4.36. Firms should be prepared to demonstrate to their competent authority that the use of a particular innovative solution is appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93734: 4.37. Firms may wish to refer to the ESAs' 2018 Joint Opinion on the use of innovative solutions in the customer due diligence process, which has further detail on these points.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93735: Establishing the nature and purpose of the business relationship

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93736: 4.38. The measures firms take to establish the nature and purpose of the business relationship should be commensurate to the risk associated with the relationship and sufficient to enable

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:32]
PARAGRAPH_93737: 8 Regulation (EU) 2016/679 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 27 April 2016 on the protection of natural persons with regard to the processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data, and repealing Directive 95/46/EC (General Data Protection Regulation), ( OJ L 119, 4.5.2016, p. 1).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93739: the firm to understand who the customer is, and who the customer's beneficial owners are. Firms should at least take steps to understand:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93740: a) The nature of the customer's activities or business;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93741: b) Why the customer has chosen the firm's products and services;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93742: c) The value and sources of funds that will be flowing through the account;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93743: d) How the customer will be using the firm's products and services;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93744: e) Whether the customer has other business relationships with other parts of the firm or its wider group, and the extent to which this affects the firm's understanding of the customer; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93745: f) What constitutes 'normal' behaviour for this customer or category of customers.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93746: 4.39. Firms should refer to the risk factors in guidelines 2.4 to 2.6 of these guidelines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93747: Simplified customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93748: 4.40. To the extent permitted by national legislation, firms may apply SDD measures in situations where the ML/TF risk associated with a business relationship has been assessed as low. SDD is not an exemption from any of the CDD measures; however, firms may adjust the amount, timing or type of each or all of the CDD measures in a way that is commensurate to the low risk they have identified.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93749: 4.41. SDD measures firms may apply include but are not limited to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93750: a) the timing of CDD, for example where the product or transaction sought has features that limit its use for ML/TF purposes, for example by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33]
PARAGRAPH_93751: i. verifying the customer's or beneficial owner's identity during the establishment of the business relationship; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93752: ii. verifying the customer's or beneficial owner's identity once transactions exceed a defined threshold or once a reasonable time limit has lapsed. Firms must make sure that:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:33] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93753: a. this does not result in a de facto exemption from CDD, that is, firms must ensure that the customer's or beneficial owner's identity will ultimately be verified;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93755: b. the threshold or time limit is set at a reasonably low level (although, with regard to terrorist financing, firms should note that a low threshold alone may not be enough to reduce risk);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93756: c. they have systems in place to detect when the threshold or time limit has been reached; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93757: d. they do not defer CDD or delay obtaining relevant information about the customer where applicable legislation, for example Regulation (EU) 2015/847 or provisions in national legislation, require that this information be obtained at the outset.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93758: b) adjusting the quantity of information obtained for identification, verification or monitoring purposes, for example by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93759: i. verifying identity on the basis of information obtained from one reliable, credible and independent document or data source only; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93760: ii. assuming the nature and purpose of the business relationship because the product is designed for one particular use only, such as a company pension scheme or a shopping center gift card.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93761: c) adjusting the quality or source of information obtained for identification, verification or monitoring purposes, for example by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93762: i. accepting information obtained from the customer rather than an independent source when verifying the beneficial owner's identity (note that this is not permitted for the verification of the customer's identity); or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93763: ii. where the risk associated with all aspects of the relationship is very low, relying on the source of funds to meet some of the CDD requirements, for example where the funds are state benefit payments or where the funds have been transferred from an account in the customer's name at an EEA firm;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93764: d) adjusting the frequency of CDD updates and reviews of the business relationship, for example carrying these out only when trigger events occur such as the when the customer looks to take out a new product or service or when a certain transaction threshold is reached; firms must make sure that this does not result in a de facto exemption from keeping CDD information up-to-date.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:34]
PARAGRAPH_93765: e) adjusting the frequency and intensity of transaction monitoring, for example by monitoring transactions above a certain threshold only. Where firms choose to

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93767: do this, they must ensure that the threshold is set at a reasonable level and that they have systems in place to identify linked transactions that, together, would exceed that threshold.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93768: 4.42. Title II lists additional SDD measures that may be of particular relevance in different sectors.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93769: 4.43. The information a firm obtains when applying SDD measures must enable the firm to be reasonably satisfied that its assessment that the risk associated with the relationship is low is justified. It must also be sufficient to give the firm enough information about the nature of the business relationship to identify any unusual or suspicious transactions. SDD does not exempt an institution from reporting suspicious transactions to the FIU.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93770: 4.44. Where there are indications that the risk may not be low, for example where there are grounds to suspect that ML/TF is being attempted or where the firm has doubts about the veracity of the information obtained, SDD must not be applied.9 Equally, where specific high- risk scenarios apply and there is an obligation to conduct EDD, SDD must not be applied.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93771: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93772: 4.45. Pursuant to Articles 18 to 24 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms must apply EDD measures in higher risk situations to manage and mitigate those risks appropriately. EDD measures cannot be substituted for regular CDD measures but must be applied in addition to regular CDD measures.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93773: 4.46. Directive (EU) 2015/849 lists specific cases that firms must always treat as higher risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93774: a) where the customer, or the customer's beneficial owner, is a PEP (Articles 20 to 24);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93775: b) where a firm enters into a correspondent relationship involving the execution of payments with a third-country institution (Article 19);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93776: c) where a firm maintains a business relationship or carries out a transaction involving high-risk third countries (Article 18(1)); and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93777: d) all transactions that are

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93778: i. complex;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93779: ii. unusually large;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93780: iii. conducted in an unusual pattern; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:35]
PARAGRAPH_93781: 9 Article 11(e) and (f) and Article 15(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93783: iv. without obvious economic or lawful purpose (Article 18(2)).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93784: 4.47. Directive (EU) 2015/849 sets out specific EDD measures that firms must apply:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93785: a) where the customer, or the customer's beneficial owner, is a PEP;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93786: b) where the business relationship or transaction involves a high risk third country identified by the Commission pursuant to Article 9(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93787: c) with respect to correspondent relationships involving the execution of payments with respondents from third countries; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93788: d) with respect to all transactions that are either complex, unusually large, conducted in an unusual pattern or do not have an apparent economic or lawful purpose.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93789: Firms should apply additional EDD measures in those situations where this is commensurate to the ML/TF risk they have identified.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36]
PARAGRAPH_93790: Politically Exposed Persons

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93791: 4.48. When putting in place risk-sensitive policies and procedures to identify PEPs, firms should have regard to the list of prominent public functions published by the Commission pursuant to Article 20a(3) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 and ensure that holders of these functions are identified. This list applies to prominent functions in the EU; when determining how to identify PEPs from third countries, firms should instead refer to the list of functions in Article 3(9) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 and adjust this list on a case-by-case basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93792: 4.49. Firms that use commercially available PEP lists should ensure that information on these lists is up to date and that they understand the limitations of those lists. Firms should take additional measures where necessary, for example in situations where the screening results are inconclusive or not in line with the firm's expectations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93793: 4.50. Firms that have identified that a customer or beneficial owner is a PEP must always:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:36] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93794: a) Take adequate measures to establish the source of wealth and the source of funds to be used in the business relationship in order to allow the firm to satisfy itself that it does not handle the proceeds from corruption or other criminal activity. The measures firms should take to establish the PEP's source of wealth and the source of funds will depend on the degree of high risk associated with the business relationship. Firms should verify the source of wealth and the source of funds on the basis of reliable and independent data, documents or information where the risk associated with the PEP relationship is particularly high.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93796: b) Obtain senior management approval for entering into, or continuing, a business relationship with a PEP. The appropriate level of seniority for sign-off should be determined by the level of increased risk associated with the business relationship, and the senior manager approving a PEP business relationship should have sufficient seniority and oversight to take informed decisions on issues that directly impact the firm's risk profile.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93797: c) When considering whether to approve a PEP relationship, senior management should base their decision on the level of ML/TF risk the firm would be exposed to if it entered into that business relationship and how well equipped the firm is to manage that risk effectively.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93798: d) Apply enhanced ongoing monitoring of both transactions and the risk associated with the business relationship. Firms should identify unusual transactions and regularly review the information they hold to ensure that any new or emerging information that could affect the risk assessment is identified in a timely fashion. The frequency of ongoing monitoring should be determined by the level of high risk associated with the relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93799: 4.51. Pursuant to Article 20(b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms must apply all of these measures to PEPs, their family members and known close associates and should adjust the extent of these measures on a risk-sensitive basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93800: 4.52. Firms should ensure that the measures they put in place to comply with the Directive (EU) 2015/849and with these guidelines in respect of PEPs do not result in PEP customers being unduly denied access to financial services.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93801: High-risk third countries

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93802: 4.53. With respect to a business relationship or transaction involving high-risk third countries as set out in Article 9(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should ensure that they apply, as a minimum, the EDD measures set out in Article 18a(1) and, where applicable, the measures set out in Article 18 a(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93803: 4.54. Firms should apply the measures listed in guideline 4.53 and should adjust the extent of these measures on a risk-sensitive basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93804: 4.55. A business relationship or transaction always involves a high risk third country if

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93805: a) the funds were generated in a high risk third country;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93806: b) the funds are received from a high risk third country;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:37]
PARAGRAPH_93807: c) the destination of funds is a high risk third country;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93809: d) the firm is dealing with a natural person or legal entity resident or established in a high risk third country; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93810: e) the firm is dealing with a trustee established in a high risk third country or with a trust governed under the law of a high risk third country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93811: 4.56. When performing CDD measures or during the course of a business relationship, firms should ensure that they also apply the EDD measures set out in Article 18a(1) and, where applicable, the measures set out in Article 18a(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, where firms determine that

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93812: a) the transaction passes through a high-risk third country, for example because of where the intermediary payment services provider is based; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93813: b) a customer's beneficial owner is resident in a high-risk third country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93814: 4.57. Notwithstanding guidelines 4.54 and 4.56, firms should carefully assess the risk associated with business relationships and transactions where

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93815: a) the customer is known to maintain close personal or professional links with a high-risk third country; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93816: b) beneficial owner(s) is/are known to maintain close personal or professional links with a high-risk third country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93817: In those situations, firms should take a risk-based decision on whether or not to apply the measures listed in Article 18a) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, EDD measures or regular CDD measures.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93818: Correspondent relationships

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93819: 4.58. To comply with Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms must take specific EDD measures where they have a cross-border correspondent relationship with a respondent based in a third country. Firms must apply all of these measures and should adjust the extent of these measures on a risk-sensitive basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93820: 4.59. Firms should refer to Title II for guidelines on EDD in relation to correspondent banking relationships; these guidelines may also be useful for firms in other correspondent relationships.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38]
PARAGRAPH_93821: Unusual transactions

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:38] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93822: 4.60. Firms should put in place adequate policies and procedures to detect unusual transactions or patterns of transactions. Where a firm detects such transactions, it must apply EDD measures. Transactions may be unusual because:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93824: a) they are larger than what the firm would normally expect based on its knowledge of the customer, the business relationship or the category to which the customer belongs;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93825: b) they have an unusual or unexpected pattern compared with the customer's normal activity or the pattern of transactions associated with similar customers, products or services; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93826: c) they are very complex compared with other, similar, transactions associated with similar customer types, products or services, and the firm is not aware of an economic rationale or lawful purpose or doubts the veracity of the information it has been given.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93827: 4.61. These EDD measures should enable the firm to determine whether these transactions give rise to suspicion and must at least include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93828: a) taking reasonable and adequate measures to understand the background and purpose of these transactions, for example by establishing the source and destination of the funds or finding out more about the customer's business to ascertain the likelihood of the customer making such transactions; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93829: b) monitoring the business relationship and subsequent transactions more frequently and with greater attention to detail. A firm may decide to monitor individual transactions where this is commensurate to the risk it has identified.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93830: Other high-risk situations

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93831: 4.62. In all other high risk situations, firms should take an informed decision about which EDD measures are appropriate for each high-risk situation. The appropriate type of EDD, including the extent of the additional information sought, and of the increased monitoring carried out, will depend on the reason why an occasional transaction or a business relationship was classified as high risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93832: 4.63. Firms are not required to apply all the EDD measures listed below in all cases. For example, in certain high-risk situations it may be appropriate to focus on enhanced ongoing monitoring during the course of the business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93833: 4.64. EDD measures firms should apply may include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93834: a) Increasing the quantity of information obtained for CDD purposes as follows:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:39]
PARAGRAPH_93835: i. Information about the customer's or beneficial owner's identity, or the customer's ownership and control structure, to be satisfied that the risk associated with the relationship is well understood. This may include obtaining and assessing information about the customer's or beneficial owner's reputation

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93837: and assessing any negative allegations against the customer or beneficial owner. Examples include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93838: a. information about family members and close business partners;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93839: b. information about the customer's or beneficial owner's past and present business activities; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93840: c. adverse media searches.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93841: ii. Information about the intended nature of the business relationship to ascertain that the nature and purpose of the business relationship is legitimate and to help firms obtain a more complete customer risk profile. This may include obtaining information on:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93842: a. the number, size and frequency of transactions that are likely to pass through the account, to enable the firm to spot deviations that might give rise to suspicion (in some cases, requesting evidence may be appropriate);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93843: b. why the customer is looking for a specific product or service, in particular where it is unclear why the customer's needs cannot be met better in another way, or in a different jurisdiction;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93844: c. the destination of funds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93845: d. the nature of the customer's or beneficial owner's business, to enable the firm to better understand the likely nature of the business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93846: b) Increasing the quality of information obtained for CDD purposes to confirm the customer's or beneficial owner's identity including by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93847: i. requiring the first payment to be carried out through an account verifiably in the customer's name with a bank subject to CDD standards that are not less robust than those set out in Chapter II of Directive (EU) 2015/849; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:40]
PARAGRAPH_93848: ii. establishing that the customer's wealth and the funds that are used in the business relationship are not the proceeds of criminal activity and that the source of wealth and source of funds are consistent with the firm's knowledge of the customer and the nature of the business relationship. In some cases, where the risk associated with the relationship is particularly high, verifying the source of wealth and the

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93850: source of funds may be the only adequate risk mitigation tool. The source of funds or wealth can be verified, inter alia, by reference to VAT and income tax returns, copies of audited accounts, pay slips, public deeds or independent media reports. Firms should have regard to the fact that funds from legitimate business activity may still constitute money laundering or terrorist financing as set out in paragraphs (3) to (5) of Article 1 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93851: c) Increasing the frequency of reviews to be satisfied that the firm continues to be able to manage the risk associated with the individual business relationship or conclude that the relationship no longer corresponds to the firm's risk appetite, and to help identify any transactions that require further review, including by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93852: i. increasing the frequency of reviews of the business relationship to ascertain whether the customer's risk profile has changed and whether the risk remains manageable;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93853: ii. obtaining the approval of senior management to commence or continue the business relationship to ensure that senior management are aware of the risk their firm is exposed to and can take an informed decision about the extent to which they are equipped to manage that risk;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93854: iii. reviewing the business relationship on a more regular basis to ensure any changes to the customer's risk profile are identified, assessed and, where necessary, acted upon; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93855: iv. conducting more frequent or in-depth transaction monitoring to identify any unusual or unexpected transactions that might give rise to suspicion of ML/TF. This may include establishing the destination of funds or ascertaining the reason for certain transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41]
PARAGRAPH_93856: 4.65. Title II lists additional EDD measures that may be of particular relevance in different sectors. Other considerations

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93857: 4.66. Firms should not enter into a business relationship if they are unable to comply with their CDD requirements, if they are not satisfied that the purpose and nature of the business relationship are legitimate or if they are not satisfied that they can effectively manage the risk that they may be used for ML/TF purposes. Where such a business relationship already exists, firms should terminate it or suspend transactions until it can be terminated, subject to instructions from law enforcement, where applicable.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:41] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93858: 4.67. Where firms have reasonable grounds to suspect that ML/TF is being attempted, firms must report this to their FIU.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93860: 4.68. Firms should note that the application of a risk-based approach does not of itself require them to refuse, or terminate, business relationships with entire categories of customers that they associate with higher ML/TF risk, as the risk associated with individual business relationships will vary, even within one category.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93861: Monitoring

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93862: 4.69. Pursuant to Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should monitor their business relationships with their customers.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93863: 4.70. Monitoring should include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93864: a. Monitoring of transactions to ensure that these are in line with the customer's risk profile, their financial situation, and the firm's wider knowledge of the customer to detect unusual or suspicious transactions; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93865: b. keeping the documents, data or information they hold up to date, with a view to understanding whether the risk associated with the business relationship has changed and to ascertain that the information that forms the basis for ongoing monitoring is accurate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93866: 4.71. Firms should determine the frequency and intensity of monitoring on a risk-sensitive basis, taking into account the nature, size and complexity of their business and the level of risk to which they are exposed.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93867: Transaction monitoring

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93868: 4.72. Firms should ensure that their approach to transaction monitoring is effective and appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93869: 4.73. An effective transaction monitoring system relies on up-to-date customer information and should enable the firm reliably to identify unusual and suspicious transactions and transaction patterns. Firms should ensure that they have processes in place to review flagged transactions without undue delay.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93870: 4.74. What is appropriate will depend on the nature, size and complexity of the firm's business, as well as the risk to which the firm is exposed. Firms should adjust the intensity and frequency of monitoring in line with the risk-based approach. Firms should in any case determine.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93871: a) Which transactions they will monitor in real time, and which transactions they will monitor ex-post. As part of this, firms should determine:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:42]
PARAGRAPH_93872: i. which high-risk factors, or combination of high-risk factors, will always trigger real-time monitoring; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93874: ii. which transactions associated with higher ML/TF risk are monitored in real time, in particular those where the risk associated with the business relationship is already increased;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93875: b) Whether they will monitor transactions manually or using an automated transaction monitoring system. Firms that process a high volume of transaction should consider putting in place an automated transaction monitoring system; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93876: c) The frequency of transaction monitoring, taking into account the requirements in these guidelines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93877: 4.75. In addition to real time and ex-post monitoring of individual transactions, and irrespective of the level of automation used, firms should regularly perform ex-post reviews on a sample taken from all processed transactions to identify trends that could inform their risk assessments and to test and, if necessary, subsequently improve the reliability and appropriateness of their transaction monitoring system. Firms should also use the information obtained under Guidelines 1.29 to 1.30 to test and improve their transaction monitoring system.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93878: Keeping CDD information up to date

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93879: 4.76. Firms must keep CDD information up to date.10

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93880: 4.77. When putting in place policies and procedures to keep CDD information up to date, firms should pay particular attention to the need to remain alert to, and capture, information about the customer that will help them understand whether the risk associated with the business relationship has changed. Examples of the information firms should capture include an apparent change in the source of the customer's funds, the customer's ownership structure, or behaviour that is consistently out of line with the behaviour or transaction profile the firm had expected.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93881: 4.78. A change in the customer's circumstances is likely to trigger a requirement to apply CDD measures to that customer. In those situations, firms may not need to re-apply all CDD measures, but should determine which CDD measures to apply, and the extent of the CDD measures they will apply. For example, in lower risk cases, firms may be able to draw on information obtained in the course of the business relationship to update the CDD information they hold on the customer.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93882: Guideline 5: Record-keeping

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:43]
PARAGRAPH_93883: 10 Article 14(5) of the AMLD

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93885: 5.1. For the purpose of Articles 8 and 40 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms must keep records at least of

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93886: a) CDD information;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93887: b) Their risk assessments; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93888: c) Transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93889: 5.2. Firms should ensure that these records are sufficient to demonstrate to their competent authority that the measures taken are adequate in view of the ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93890: Guideline 6: Training

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93891: 6.1. Firms must make their staff aware of the provisions they have put in place to comply with their AML/CFT obligations.11

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93892: 6.2. As part of this, and in line with guidance contained in Title I, firms should take steps to ensure that staff understand

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93893: a) The business-wide risk assessment, and how it affects their daily work;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93894: b) The firm's AML/CFT policies and procedures, and how they have to be applied; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93895: c) How to recognise suspicious or unusual transactions and activities, and how to proceed in such cases.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93896: 6.3. Firms should ensure that AML/CFT training is

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93897: a) Relevant to the firm and its business;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93898: b) Tailored to staff and their specific roles;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93899: c) Updated regularly; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93900: d) Effective.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93901: Guideline 7: Reviewing effectiveness

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93902: 7.1. Firms should regularly assess the effectiveness of their approach to AML/CFT and determine the frequency and intensity of such assessments on a risk-sensitive basis, taking into account the nature and size of their business and the level of ML/TF risk to which they are exposed.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:44]
PARAGRAPH_93903: 11 Article 46(1) of Directive (EU) 2015/849

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:45]
PARAGRAPH_93905: 7.2. Firms should consider whether an independent review of their approach may be warranted or required.12

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:45]
PARAGRAPH_93906: 12 Article 8(4)(b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:46]
PARAGRAPH_93908: Title II: Sector-specific Guidelines

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:46]
PARAGRAPH_93909: The sector-specific guidelines in Title II complement the general guidance in Title I of these guidelines. They should be read in conjunction with Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:46]
PARAGRAPH_93910: The risk factors described in each sectoral guideline of Title II are not exhaustive. Firms should take a holistic view of the risk associated with the situation and note that isolated risk factors do not necessarily move a business relationship or occasional transaction into a higher or lower risk category.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:46]
PARAGRAPH_93911: Each sectoral guideline in Title II also sets out examples of the CDD measures firms should apply on a risk-sensitive basis in high-risk and, to the extent permitted by national legislation, low risk situations. These examples are not exhaustive and firms should decide on the most appropriate CDD measures in line with the level and type of ML/TF risk they have identified.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93913: Guideline 8: Sectoral guideline for correspondent relationships

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93914: 8.1. Guideline 8 provides guidelines on correspondent banking as defined in Article 3(8)(a) of Directive (EU) 2015/849. Firms offering other correspondent relationships as defined in Article 3(8)(b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 should apply these guidelines as appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93915: 8.2. Firms should take into account that, in a correspondent banking relationship, the correspondent provides banking services to the respondent, either in a principal-to- principal capacity or on the respondent's customers' behalf. The correspondent does not normally have a business relationship with the respondent's customers and will not normally know their identity or the nature or purpose of the underlying transaction, unless this information is included in the payment instruction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93916: 8.3. Firms should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93917: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93918: Product, service and transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93919: 8.4. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93920: a) The account can be used by other respondent banks that have a direct relationship with the respondent but not with the correspondent ('nesting', or downstream clearing), which means that the correspondent is indirectly providing services to other banks that are not the respondent.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93921: b) The account can be used by other entities within the respondent's group that have not themselves been subject to the correspondent's due diligence.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93922: c) The service includes the opening of a payable-through account, which allows the respondent's customers to carry out transactions directly on the account of the respondent.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93923: 8.5. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93924: a) The relationship is limited to a SWIFT Risk Management Application (RMA) capability, which is designed to manage communications between financial institutions. In a SWIFT RMA relationship, the respondent, or counterparty, does not have a payment account relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:47]
PARAGRAPH_93925: b) Banks are acting in a principal-to-principal capacity, rather than processing transactions on behalf of their underlying clients, for example in the case of foreign exchange services between two banks where the business is transacted

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93927: on a principal- to-principal basis between the banks and where the settlement of a transaction does not involve a payment to a third party. In those cases, the transaction is for the own account of the respondent bank.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93928: c) The transaction relates to the selling, buying or pledging of securities on regulated markets, for example when acting as or using a custodian with direct access, usually through a local participant, to an EU or non-EU securities settlement system.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93929: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93930: 8.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93931: a) The respondent's AML/CFT policies and the systems and controls the respondent has in place to implement them fall short of the standards required by Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93932: b) The respondent is not subject to adequate AML/CFT supervision.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93933: c) The respondent, its parent or a firm belonging to the same group as the respondent has recently been the subject of regulatory enforcement for inadequate AML/CFT policies and procedures and/or breaches of AML/CFT obligations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93934: d) The respondent conducts significant business with sectors that are associated with higher levels of ML/TF risk; for example, the respondent conducts significant remittance business or business on behalf of certain money remitters or exchange houses, with non-residents or in a currency other than that of the country in which it is based.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93935: e) The respondent's management or ownership includes PEPs, in particular where a PEP can exert meaningful influence over the respondent, where the PEP's reputation, integrity or suitability as a member of the management board or key function holder gives rise to concern or where the PEP is from a jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to those jurisdictions where corruption is perceived to be systemic or widespread.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:48]
PARAGRAPH_93936: f) The history of the business relationship with the respondent gives rise to concern, for example because the amount of transactions is not in line with what the correspondent would expect based on its knowledge of the nature and size of the respondent.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93938: g) The respondent's failure to provide the information requested by the correspondent for CDD and EDD purposes, and information on the payer or the payee that is required under Regulation (EU) 2015/847. For this purpose, the correspondent should consider the quantitative and qualitative criteria set out in the Joint Guidelines JC/GL/2017/16.13

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93939: 8.7. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk. The correspondent is satisfied that :

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93940: a) the respondent's AML/CFT controls are not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93941: b) the respondent is part of the same group as the correspondent, is not based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk and complies effectively with group AML standards that are not less strict than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93942: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93943: 8.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93944: a) The respondent is based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to those jurisdictions:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93945: i. identified as high-risk third countries pursuant to Article 9(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93946: ii. with significant levels of corruption and/or other predicate offences to money laundering;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93947: iii. without adequate capacity of the legal and judicial system effectively to prosecute those offences;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93948: iv. with significant levels of terrorist financing or terrorists activities; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93949: V. without effective AML/CFT supervision.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93950: b) The respondent conducts significant business with customers based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93951: c) The respondent's parent is headquartered or is incorporated in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:49]
PARAGRAPH_93952: 13 Joint Guidelines under Article 25 of Regulation (EU) 2015/847 on the measures payment service providers should take to detect missing or incomplete information on the payer or the payee, and the procedures they should put in place to manage a transfer of funds lacking the required information issued on 22 September 2017.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93954: 8.9. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93955: a) The respondent is based in an EEA member country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93956: ) The respondent is based in a third country that has AML/CFT requirements not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849 and effectively implements those requirements (although correspondents should note that this does not exempt them from applying EDD measures set out in Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93958: 8.10. All correspondents should carry out CDD measures set out in Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 on the respondent, who is the correspondent's customer, on a risk-sensitive basis. This means that correspondents should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93959: a) Identify, and verify the identity of, the respondent and its beneficial owner. As part of this, correspondents should obtain sufficient information about the respondent's business and reputation to establish that the money-laundering risk associated with the respondent is not increased. In particular, correspondents should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93960: i. obtain information about the respondent's management and consider the relevance, for financial crime prevention purposes, of any links the respondent's management or ownership might have to PEPs or other high-risk individuals; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50]
PARAGRAPH_93961: ii. consider, on a risk-sensitive basis, whether obtaining information about the respondent's major business, the types of customers it attracts, and the quality of its AML systems and controls (including publicly available information about any recent regulatory or criminal sanctions for AML failings) would be appropriate. Where the respondent is a branch, subsidiary or affiliate, correspondents should also consider the status, reputation and AML controls of the parent.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93962: b) Establish and document the nature and purpose of the service provided, as well as the responsibilities of each institution. This may include setting out, in writing, the scope of the relationship, which products and services will be supplied, and how and by whom the correspondent banking facility can be used (e.g. if it can be used by other banks through their relationship with the respondent).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:50] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93963: c) Monitor the business relationship, including transactions, to identify changes in the respondent's risk profile and detect unusual or suspicious behaviour, including activities that are not consistent with the purpose of the services provided or that are contrary to commitments that have been concluded between the correspondent and the respondent. Where the correspondent

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51]
PARAGRAPH_93965: bank allows the respondent's customers direct access to accounts (e.g. payable-through accounts, or nested accounts), it should conduct enhanced ongoing monitoring of the business relationship. Owing to the nature of correspondent banking, post-execution monitoring is the norm.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93966: d) Ensure that the CDD information they hold is up to date.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93967: 8.11. Correspondents must also establish that the respondent does not permit its accounts to be used by a shell bankin line with Article 24 of Directive (EU) 2015/849. This may include asking the respondent for confirmation that it does not deal with shell banks, having sight of relevant passages in the respondent's policies and procedures, or considering publicly available information, such as legal provisions that prohibit the servicing of shell banks.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51]
PARAGRAPH_93968: 8.12. There is no requirement in Directive (EU) 2015/849 for correspondents to apply CDD measures to the respondent's individual customers.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93969: 8.13. Correspondents should take into account that CDD questionnaires provided by international organisations are not normally designed specifically to help correspondents comply with their obligations under Directive (EU) 2015/849. When considering whether to use these questionnaires, correspondents should assess whether they will be sufficient to allow them to comply with their obligations under Directive (EU) 2015/849 and should take additional steps where necessary.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51]
PARAGRAPH_93970: Respondents based in non-EEA countries

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51]
PARAGRAPH_93971: 8.14. To discharge their obligation under Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, where the correspondent relationship involves the execution of payments with a third country respondent institution, correspondents should apply specific EDD measures in addition to the CDD measures set out in Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 but can adjust those measures on a risk sensitive basis. In all other situations, firms should apply at least guideline 8.10 to 8.13.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93972: 8.15. Correspondents must apply each of these EDD measures to respondents based in a non-EEA country, but correspondents can adjust the extent of these measures on a risk- sensitive basis.
