For example, if the correspondent is satisfied, based on adequate research, that the respondent is based in a third country that has an effective AML/CFT regime, supervised effectively for compliance with these requirements, and that there are no grounds to suspect that the respondent's AML/CFT policies and procedures are, or have recently been deemed, inadequate, then the assessment of the respondent's controls may not necessarily have to be carried out in full detail.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:51]
PARAGRAPH_93973: 8.16. Correspondents should always adequately document their CDD and EDD measures and decision-making processes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93975: 8.17. To comply with Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, the risk-sensitive measures firms take should enable them to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93976: a) Gather sufficient information about a respondent institution to understand fully the nature of the respondent's business, in order to establish the extent to which the respondent's business exposes the correspondent to higher money-laundering risk. This should include taking steps to understand and risk-assess the nature of respondent's customer base, if necessary by asking the respondent about its customers, and the type of activities that the respondent will transact through the correspondent account.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93977: b) Determine from publicly available information the reputation of the institution and the quality of supervision. This means that the correspondent should assess the extent to which the correspondent can take comfort from the fact that the respondent is adequately supervised for compliance with its AML obligations. A number of publicly available resources, for example FATF or FSAP assessments, which contain sections on effective supervision, may help correspondents establish this.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93978: c) Assess the respondent institution's AML/CFT controls. This implies that the correspondent should carry out a qualitative assessment of the respondent's AML/CFT control framework, not just obtain a copy of the respondent's AML policies and procedures. This assessment should be documented appropriately. In line with the risk-based approach, where the risk is especially high and in particular where the volume of correspondent banking transactions is substantive, the correspondent should consider on-site visits and/or sample testing to be satisfied that the respondent's AML policies and procedures are implemented effectively.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52]
PARAGRAPH_93979: d) Obtain approval from senior management, as defined in Article 3(12) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 before establishing new correspondent relationships and where material new risks emerge, such as because the country in which the respondent is based is designated as high risk under provisions in Article 9 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 .. The approving senior manager should not be the officer sponsoring the relationship and the higher the risk associated with the relationship, the more senior the approving senior manager should be. Correspondents should keep senior management informed of high-risk correspondent banking relationships and the steps the correspondent takes to manage that risk effectively.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:52]
PARAGRAPH_93980: e) Document the responsibilities of each institution. If not already specified in its standard agreement, the correspondents should conclude a written agreement including at least the following:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93982: i. the products and services provided to the respondent,

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93983: ii. how and by whom the correspondent banking facility can be used (e.g. if it can be used by other banks through their relationship with the respondent), what the respondent's AML/CFT responsibilities are;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93984: iii. how the correspondent will monitor the relationship to ascertain the respondent complies with its responsibilities under this agreement ( for example through ex post transaction monitoring);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93985: iv. the information that should be supplied by the respondent at the correspondent's request (in particular for the purpose of monitoring the correspondent relationship) and a reasonable deadline by which the information should be provided (taking into account the complexity of the payment chain or the correspondent chain) .

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93986: f) With respect to payable-through accounts and nested accounts, be satisfied that the respondent credit or financial institution has verified the identity of and performed ongoing due diligence on the customer having direct access to accounts of the correspondent and that it is able to provide relevant CDD data to the correspondent institution upon request. Correspondents should seek to obtain confirmation from the respondent that the relevant data can be provided upon request.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93987: Respondents based in EEA countries

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93988: 8.18. Where the respondent is based in an EEA country, Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 does not apply. The correspondent is, however, still obliged to apply risk-sensitive CDD measures pursuant to Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93989: 8.19. Where the risk associated with a respondent based in an EEA Member State is increased, correspondents must apply EDD measures in line with Article 18 of Directive (EU) 2015/849. In that case, correspondents should consider applying at least some of the EDD measures described in Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, in particular Article 19(a) and (b).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93990: Respondents established in high-risk third countries, and correspondent relationships involving high-risk third countries

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53]
PARAGRAPH_93991: 8.20. Correspondents should determine which of their relationships involve high-risk third countries, identified pursuant to Article 9(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:53] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93992: 8.21. Correspondents should also, as part of their standard CDD measures, determine the likelihood of the respondent initiating transactions involving high-risk third countries, including where a significant proportion of the respondent's own customers maintain relevant professional or personal links to high-risk third countries.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93994: 8.22. To discharge their obligation under Article 18a, firms should ensure that they also apply Article 13 and 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93995: 8.23. Unless the correspondent has assessed ML/TF risk arising from the relationship with the respondent as particularly high correspondents should be able to comply with the requirements in Article 18a(1) by applying Article 13 and 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93996: 8.24. To discharge their obligation under Article 18a(1)(c) of Directive (EU)2015/849, correspondents should apply guideline 8.17(c) and take care to assess the adequacy of the respondent's policies and procedures to establish their customers' source of funds and source of wealth, carry out onsite visits or sample checks, or ask the respondent to provide evidence of the legitimate origin of a particular customer's source of wealth or source of funds, as required.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_93997: 8.25. Where Members States require firms to apply additional measures in line with article 18a)(2)correspondents should apply one or more of the following:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_93998: a) Increasing the frequency of reviews of CDD information held on the respondent, and the risk assessment of that respondent;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_93999: b) Requiring a more in-depth assessment of the respondent's AML/CFT controls. In these higher risk situations, correspondents should consider reviewing the independent audit report of the respondent's AML/CFT controls, interviewing the compliance officers, commissioning a third party review or conducting an onsite visit.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_94000: c) Requiring increased and more intrusive monitoring. Real-time monitoring of transactions is one of the EDD measures banks should consider in situations where the ML/TF risk is particularly increased. As part of this, correspondents should consider maintaining an ongoing dialogue with the respondent to develop a better understanding of the risks associated with the correspondent relationship and facilitate the rapid exchange of meaningful information, if necessary.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_94001: d) Requiring increased monitoring on transfers of funds to ensure detection of missing or incomplete information on the payer and or the payee under Regulation (EU) 2015/847 and in line with the Joint Guidelines JC/GL/2017/16.14

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_94002: e) Limiting business relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries in terms of nature, volume or means of payment, after a thorough assessment of the residual risk posed by the correspondent relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:54]
PARAGRAPH_94003: 14 Joint Guidelines under Article 25 of Regulation (EU) 2015/847 on the measures payment service providers should take to detect missing or incomplete information on the payer or the payee, and the procedures they should put in place to manage a transfer of funds lacking the required information issued on 22 September 2017 (JC/GL/2017/16).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94005: Guideline 9: Sectoral guideline for retail banks

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94006: 9.1. For the purpose of these guidelines, retail banking means the provision of banking services to natural persons and small and medium-sized enterprises. Examples of retail banking products and services include current accounts, mortgages, savings accounts, consumer and term loans, and credit lines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94007: 9.2. Owing to the nature of the products and services offered, the relative ease of access and the often large volume of transactions and business relationships, retail banking is vulnerable to terrorist financing and to all stages of the money laundering process. At the same time, the volume of business relationships and transactions associated with retail banking can make identifying ML/TF risk associated with individual relationships and spotting suspicious transactions particularly challenging.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94008: 9.3. Banks should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. Banks that provide payment initiation services or account information services should also refer to the sectoral guideline 18.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94009: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94010: Product, service and transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94011: 9.4. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94012: a) the product's features favour anonymity;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94013: b) the product allows payments from third parties that are neither associated with the product nor identified upfront, where such payments would not be expected, for example for mortgages or loans;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94014: c) the product places no restrictions on turnover, cross-border transactions or similar product features;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94015: d) new products and new business practices, including new delivery mechanisms, and the use of new or developing technologies for both new and existing products where these are not yet well understood;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94016: e) lending (including mortgages) secured against the value of assets in other jurisdictions, particularly countries where it is difficult to ascertain whether the customer has legitimate title to the collateral, or where the identities of parties guaranteeing the loan are hard to verify;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94017: f) an unusually high volume or large value of transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:55]
PARAGRAPH_94018: 9.5. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk: -

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94020: a) The product has limited functionality, for example in the case of:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94021: i. a fixed term savings product with low savings thresholds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94022: ii. a product where the benefits cannot be realised for the benefit of a third party;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94023: iii. a product where the benefits are only realisable in the long term or for a specific purpose, such as retirement or a property purchase;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94024: iv. a low-value loan facility, including one that is conditional on the purchase of a specific consumer good or service; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94025: V. a low-value product, including a lease, where the legal and beneficial title to the asset is not transferred to the customer until the contractual relationship is terminated or is never passed at all.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94026: b) The product can only be held by certain categories of customers, for example pensioners, parents on behalf of their children, or minors until they reach the age of majority.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94027: c) Transactions must be carried out through an account in the customer's name at a credit or financial institution that is subject to AML/CFT requirements that are not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94028: d) There is no overpayment facility.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94029: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94030: 9.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94031: a) The nature of the customer, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94032: i. The customer is a cash-intensive undertaking.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94033: ii. The customer is an undertaking associated with higher levels of money laundering risk, for example certain money remitters and gambling businesses.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94034: iii. The customer is an undertaking associated with a higher corruption risk, for example operating in the extractive industries or the arms trade.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94035: iv. The customer is a non-profit organisation that supports jurisdictions associated with an increased TF risk

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:56]
PARAGRAPH_94036: V. The customer is a new undertaking without an adequate business profile or track record.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94038: vi. The customer is a non-resident. Banks should note that Article 16 of Directive 2014/92/EU creates a right for consumers who are legally resident in the European Union to obtain a basic bank account, although the right to open and use a basic payment account applies only to the extent that banks can comply with their AML/CFT obligations and does not exempt banks from their obligation to identify and assess ML/TF risk, including the risk associated with the customer not being a resident of the Member State in which the bank is based. 15

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94039: vii. The customer's beneficial owner cannot easily be identified, for example because the customer's ownership structure is unusual, unduly complex or opaque, or because the customer issues bearer shares.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94040: b) The customer's behaviour, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94041: i. The customer is reluctant to provide CDD information or appears deliberately to avoid face-to-face contact.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94042: ii. The customer's evidence of identity is in a non-standard form for no apparent reason.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94043: iii. The customer's behaviour or transaction volume is not in line with that expected from the category of customer to which they belong, or is unexpected based on the information the customer provided at account opening.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94044: iv. The customer's behaviour is unusual, for example the customer unexpectedly and without reasonable explanation accelerates an agreed repayment schedule, by means either of lump sum repayments or early termination; deposits or demands payout of high-value bank notes without apparent reason; increases activity after a period of dormancy; or makes transactions that appear to have no economic rationale.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94045: 9.7. The following factor may contribute to reducing risk: ".

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94046: a) The customer is a long-standing client whose previous transactions have not given rise to suspicion or concern, and the product or service sought is in line with the customer's risk profile.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94047: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94048: 9.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:57]
PARAGRAPH_94049: 15 See the EBA's 'Opinion on the application of customer due diligence measures to customers who are asylum seekers from higher-risk third countries or territories': http://www.eba.europa.eu/documents/10180/1359456/EBA-Op-2016- 07+%28Opinion+on+Customer+Due+Diligence+on+Asylum+Seekers%29.pdf

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94051: a) The customer's funds are derived from personal or business links to jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94052: b) The payee is located in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions known to provide funding or support for terrorist activities or where groups committing terrorist offences are known to be operating, and jurisdictions subject to financial sanctions, embargoes or measures that are related to terrorism, financing of terrorism or proliferation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94053: 9.9. The following factor may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94054: a) Countries associated with the transaction have an AML/CFT regime that is not less robust than that required under Directive (EU) 2015/849 and are associated with low levels of predicate offences.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94055: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94056: 9.10. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94057: a) non-face-to-face business relationships, where no adequate additional safeguards - for example electronic signatures, electronic identification means in accordance with Regulation EU (No) 910/2014 and anti- impersonation fraud checks - are in place;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94058: b) reliance on a third party's CDD measures in situations where the bank does not have a long-standing relationship with the referring third party;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94059: c) new delivery channels that have not been tested yet.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94060: 9.11. The following factor may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94061: a) The product is available only to customers who meet specific eligibility criteria set out by national public authorities, as in the case of state benefit recipients or specific savings products for children registered in a particular Member State.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94063: 9.12. Where banks use automated systems to identify ML/TF risk associated with individual business relationships or occasional transactions and to identify suspicious transactions, they should ensure that these systems are fit for purpose in line with the criteria set out in Title I. The use of automated IT systems should never be considered a substitute for staff vigilance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:58]
PARAGRAPH_94064: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94066: 9.13. Where the risk associated with a business relationship or occasional transaction is increased, banks must apply EDD measures pursuant to Article 18 of Directive (EU) 2015/849. These may include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94067: a) Verifying the customer's and the beneficial owner's identity on the basis of more than one reliable and independent source.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94068: b) Identifying, and verifying the identity of, other shareholders who are not the customer's beneficial owner or any natural persons who have authority to operate an account or give instructions concerning the transfer of funds or the transfer of securities.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94069: c) Obtaining more information about the customer and the nature and purpose of the business relationship to build a more complete customer profile, for example by carrying out open source or adverse media searches or commissioning a third party intelligence report. Examples of the type of information banks may seek include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94070: i. the nature of the customer's business or employment;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94071: ii. the source of the customer's wealth and the source of the customer's funds that are involved in the business relationship, to be reasonably satisfied that these are legitimate;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94072: iii. the purpose of the transaction, including, where appropriate, the destination of the customer's funds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94073: iv. information on any associations the customer might have with other jurisdictions (headquarters, operating facilities, branches, etc.) and the individuals who may influence its operations; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94074: V. where the customer is based in another country, why they seek retail banking services outside their home jurisdiction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94075: d) Increasing the frequency of transaction monitoring.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94076: e) Reviewing and, where necessary, updating information and documentation held more frequently. Where the risk associated with the relationship is particularly high, banks should review the business relationship annually.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:59]
PARAGRAPH_94077: 9.14. In respect of business relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, banks should follow the guidance in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94079: Simplified customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94080: 9.15. In low-risk situations, and to the extent permitted by national legislation, banks may apply SDD measures, which may include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94081: a) for customers that are subject to a statutory licensing and regulatory regime, verifying identity based on evidence of the customer being subject to that regime, for example through a search of the regulator's public register;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94082: b) verifying the customer's and, where applicable, the beneficial owner's identities during the establishment of the business relationship in accordance with Article 14(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94083: c) assuming that a payment drawn on an account in the sole or joint name of the customer at a regulated credit or financial institution in an EEA country satisfies the requirements stipulated by Article 13(1)(a) and (b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94084: d) accepting alternative forms of identity that meet the independent and reliable source criterion in Article 13(1)(a) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, such as a letter from a government agency or other reliable public body to the customer, where there are reasonable grounds for the customer not to be able to provide standard evidence of identity and provided that there are no grounds for suspicion;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94085: e) updating CDD information only in case of specific trigger events, such as the customer requesting a new or higher risk product, or changes in the customer's behaviour or transaction profile that suggest that the risk associated with the relationship is no longer low.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94086: Pooled accounts

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94087: 9.16. Where a bank's customer opens a 'pooled account' in order to administer funds that belong to the customer's own clients, the bank should apply full CDD measures, including treating the customer's clients as the beneficial owners of funds held in the pooled account and verifying their identities.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94088: 9.17. Where there are indications that the risk associated with the business relationship is high, banks must apply EDD measures set out in Article 18 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 as appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:60]
PARAGRAPH_94089: 9.18. However, to the extent permitted by national legislation, where the risk associated with the business relationship is low and subject to the conditions set out below, a bank may apply SDD measures provided that:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94091: a) The customer is a firm that is subject to AML/CFT obligations in an EEA state or a third country with an AML/CFT regime that is not less robust than that required by Directive (EU) 2015/849, and is supervised effectively for compliance with these requirements.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94092: b) The customer is not a firm but another obliged entity that is subject to AML/CFT obligations in an EEA state and is supervised effectively for compliance with these requirements.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94093: c) The ML/TF risk associated with the business relationship is low, based on the bank's assessment of its customer's business, the types of clients the customer's business serves and the jurisdictions the customer's business is exposed to, among other considerations;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94094: d) the bank is satisfied that the customer applies robust and risk-sensitive CDD measures to its own clients and its clients' beneficial owners (it may be appropriate for the bank to take risk-sensitive measures to assess the adequacy of its customer's CDD policies and procedures, for example by liaising directly with the customer); and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94095: e) the bank has taken risk-sensitive steps to be satisfied that the customer will provide CDD information and documents on its underlying clients that are the beneficial owners of funds held in the pooled account immediately upon request, for example by including relevant provisions in a contract with the customer or by sample-testing the customer's ability to provide CDD information upon request.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94096: 9.19. Where the conditions for the application of SDD to pooled accounts are met, SDD measures may consist of the bank:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94097: a) identifying and verifying the identity of the customer, including the customer's beneficial owners (but not the customer's underlying clients);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94098: b) assessing the purpose and intended nature of the business relationship; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94099: c) conducting ongoing monitoring of the business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94100: Customers that offer services related to virtual currencies

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:61]
PARAGRAPH_94101: 9.20. Firms should take into account the fact that apart from providers engaged in exchange services between virtual currency and fiat currencies and Custodian Wallet Providers which are obliged entities under Directive (EU) 2015/849, the issuing or holding of virtual currencies as defined in point (18) of Article 3 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 remains largely unregulated

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94103: in the EU and this increases the ML/TF risks. Firms may wish to refer to the EBA's report on crypto assets of January 2019.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94104: 9.21. When entering into a business relationship with customers that provide services related to virtual currencies, firms should, as part of their ML/TF risk assessment of the customer, consider the ML/TF risk associated with virtual currencies.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94105: 9.22. Firms should consider among others the following as virtual currency businesses:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94106: a) Operating as a virtual currency trading platform that effects exchanges between fiat currency and virtual currency;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94107: b) Operating as a virtual currency trading platform that effects exchanges between virtual currencies;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94108: c) Operating as a virtual currency trading platform that allows peer-to-peer transactions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94109: d) Providing custodian wallet services;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94110: e) Arranging, advising or benefiting from 'initial coin offerings' (ICOs).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94111: 9.23. To ensure that the level of ML/TF risk associated with such customers is mitigated, banks should not apply simplified due diligence measures. At a minimum as part of their CDD measures, firms should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94112: a) Enter into dialogue with the customer to understand the nature of the business and the ML/TF risks it poses;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94113: b) In addition to verifying the identity of the customer's beneficial owners, carry out due diligence on senior management to the extent that they are different, including consideration of any adverse information ;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94114: c) Understand the extent to which these customers apply their own customer due diligence measures to their clients either under a legal obligation or on a voluntary basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94115: d) Establish whether the customer is registered or licensed in an EEA Member State, or in a third country, and take a view on the adequacy of that third country's AML/CFT regime;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:62]
PARAGRAPH_94116: e) Finding out whether businesses using ICOs in the form of virtual currencies to raise money are legitimate and, where applicable, regulated.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:63]
PARAGRAPH_94118: 9.24. Where the risk associated with such customers is increased, banks should apply EDD measures in line with Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94120: Guideline 10: Sectoral guideline for electronic money issuers

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94121: 10.1. Guideline 10 provides guidelines for electronic money issuers (e-money issuers) as defined in Article 2(3) of Directive 2009/110/EC. The level of ML/TF risk associated with electronic money as defined in Article 2(2) of Directive 2009/110/EC (e-money) depends primarily on the features of individual e-money products and the degree to which e-money issuers use other persons to distribute and redeem e-money on their behalf pursuant to Article 3(4) of Directive 2009/110/EC.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94122: 10.2. Firms that issue e-money should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. Firms whose authorisation includes the provision of business activities as payment initiation services and account information services s should also refer to the sectoral guideline 18. The sectoral guideline 11 for money remitters may also be relevant in this context.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94123: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94124: Product risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94125: 10.3. E-money issuers should consider the ML/TF risk related to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94126: a) thresholds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94127: b) the funding method; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94128: c) utility and negotiability.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94129: 10.4. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94130: a) Thresholds: the product allows

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94131: i. high-value or unlimited-value payments, loading or redemption, including cash withdrawal;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94132: ii. high number of payments, loading or redemption, including cash withdrawal;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94133: iii. high or unlimited amount of funds to be stored on the e-money product/account.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94134: b) Funding method: the product can be

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94135: i. loaded anonymously, for example with cash, anonymous e-money or e-money products that benefit from the exemption in Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:64]
PARAGRAPH_94136: ii. funded with payments from unidentified third parties;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94138: iii. funded with other e-money products.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94139: c) Utility and negotiability: the product

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94140: i. allows person-to-person transfers;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94141: ii. is accepted as a means of payment by a large number of merchants or points of sale;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94142: iii. is designed specifically to be accepted as a means of payment by merchants dealing in goods and services associated with a high risk of financial crime, for example online gambling;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94143: iv. can be used in cross-border transactions or in different jurisdictions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94144: v. is designed to be used by persons other than the customer, for example certain partner card products (but not low-value gift cards);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94145: vi. allows high-value cash withdrawals.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94146: 10.5. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94147: a) Thresholds: the product

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94148: i. sets low-value limits on payments, loading or redemption, including cash withdrawal (although firms should note that a low threshold alone may not be enough to reduce TF risk);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94149: ii. limits number of payments, loading or redemption, including cash withdrawal in a given period;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94150: iii. limits the amount of funds that can be stored on the e-money product/account at any one time.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94151: b) Funding: the product

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94152: i. requires that the funds for purchase or reloading are verifiably drawn from an account held in the customer's sole or joint name at an EEA credit or financial institution;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94153: c) Utility and negotiability: the product

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94154: i. does not allow or strictly limits cash withdrawal;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94155: ii. can be used only domestically;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:65]
PARAGRAPH_94156: iii. is accepted by a limited number of merchants or points of sale, with whose business the e-money issuer is familiar;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94158: iv. is designed specifically to restrict its use by merchants dealing in goods and services that are associated with a high risk of financial crime;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94159: v. is accepted as a means of payment for limited types of low-risk services or products.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94160: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94161: 10.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94162: a) The customer purchases several e-money products from the same issuer, frequently reloads the product or make several cash withdrawals in a short period of time and without an economic rationale; where distributors (or agents acting as distributors) are obliged entities themselves, this also applies to e-money products from different issuers purchased from the same distributor.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94163: b) The customer's transactions are always just below any value/transaction limits.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94164: c) The product appears to be used by several people whose identity is not known to the issuer (e.g. the product is used from several IP addresses at the same time).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94165: d) There are frequent changes in the customer's identification data, such as home address or IP address, or linked bank accounts.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94166: e) The product is not used for the purpose it was designed for, for example it is used overseas when it was designed as a shopping centre gift card.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94167: 10.7. The following factor may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94168: a) The product is available only to certain categories of customers, for example social benefit recipients or employees of a company that issues them to cover corporate expenses.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94169: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94170: 10.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94171: a) Online and non-face-to-face distribution without adequate safeguards, such as electronic signatures, electronic identification means meeting the criteria set out in Regulation (EU) No 910/2014 and anti-impersonation fraud measures.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:66]
PARAGRAPH_94172: b) Distribution through intermediaries that are not themselves obliged entities under Directive (EU) 2015/849 or national legislation where applicable, where the e-money issuer:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94174: i. relies on the intermediary to carry out some of the AML/CFT obligations of the e-money issuer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94175: ii. has not satisfied itself that the intermediary has in place adequate AML/CFT systems and controls; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94176: iii. segmentation of services, that is, the provision of e-money services by several operationally independent service providers without due oversight and coordination.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94177: 10.9. Firms should, prior to signing a distribution agreement with a merchant, understand the nature and purpose of the merchant's business to satisfy themselves that the goods and services provided are legitimate and to assess the ML/TF risk associated with the merchant's business. In case of an online merchant, firms should also take steps to understand the type of customers this merchant attracts, and establish the expected volume and size of transactions in order to spot suspicious or unusual transactions

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94178: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94179: 10.10. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94180: a) The payee is located in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk and/or the product has been issued or receives funds from sources in such a jurisdiction. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions known to provide funding or support for terrorist activities or where groups committing terrorist offences are known to be operating, and jurisdictions subject to financial sanctions, embargoes or measures that are related to terrorism, financing of terrorism or proliferation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94182: Customer Due Diligence measures

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94183: 10.11.Firms should apply CDD measures to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94184: a) The owner of the electronic money account or product; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94185: b) Additional card holders. Where products are linked to multiple cards, firms should establish whether they have entered into one or more business relationships, and whether additional card holders could be beneficial owners.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:67]
PARAGRAPH_94186: 10.12. National legislation may provide for an exemption from identification and verification of the customer's and beneficial owners' identities and assessment of the nature and purpose of the business relationship for certain E-money products in accordance with Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94188: 10.13.Firms should note that the exemption under Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 does not extend to the obligation to conduct ongoing monitoring of transactions and the business relationship, nor does it exempt them from the obligation to identify and report suspicious transactions; this means that firms should ensure that they obtain sufficient information about their customers, or the types of customers their product will target, to be able to carry out meaningful ongoing monitoring of the business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94189: 10.14. Examples of the types of monitoring systems firms should put in place include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94190: a) transaction monitoring systems that detect anomalies or suspicious patterns of behaviour, including the unexpected use of the product in a way for which it was not designed; the firm may be able to disable the product either manually or through on- chip controls until it has been able to satisfy itself that there are no grounds for suspicion;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94191: b) systems that identify discrepancies between submitted and detected information, for example, between submitted country of origin information and the electronically detected IP address;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94192: c) systems that compare data submitted with data held on other business relationships and that can identify patterns such as the same funding instrument or the same contact details;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94193: d) systems that identify whether the product is used with merchants dealing in goods and services that are associated with a high risk of financial crime;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94194: e) systems that link e-money products to devices or IP addresses for web-based transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94195: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94196: 10.15. To comply with Article 18a in respect of relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, e-money issuers should apply the EDD measures set out in this regard in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94197: 10.16. Examples of EDD measures firms should apply in all other high-risk situations include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94198: a) obtaining additional customer information during identification, such as the source of funds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:68]
PARAGRAPH_94199: b) applying additional verification measures from a wider variety of reliable and independent sources (e.g. checking against online databases) in order to verify the customer's or beneficial owner's identity;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94201: c) obtaining additional information about the intended nature of the business relationship, for example by asking customers about their business or the jurisdictions to which they intend to transfer E-money;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94202: d) obtaining information about the merchant/payee, in particular where the E- money issuer has grounds to suspect that its products are being used to purchase illicit or age-restricted goods;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94203: e) applying identity fraud checks to ensure that the customer is who they claim to be;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94204: f) applying enhanced monitoring to the customer relationship and individual transactions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94205: g) establishing the source and/or the destination of funds.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94206: Simplified customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94207: 10.17.To the extent permitted by national legislation, firms may consider applying SDD to low- risk e-money products that do not benefit from the exemption provided by Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94208: 10.18.To the extent permitted by national legislation, examples of SDD measures firms may apply in low-risk situations include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94209: a) postponing the verification of the customer's or beneficial owner's identity to a certain later date after the establishment of the relationship or until a certain (low) monetary threshold is exceeded (whichever occurs first). The monetary threshold should not exceed EUR 150 where the product is not reloadable or can be used in other jurisdictions or for cross-border transactions);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94210: b) verifying the customer's identity on the basis of a payment drawn on an account in the sole or joint name of the customer or an account over which the customer can be shown to have control with an EEA-regulated credit or financial institution;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94211: c) verifying identity on the basis of fewer sources;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94212: d) verifying identity on the basis of less reliable sources;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94213: e) using alternative methods to verify identity;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:69]
PARAGRAPH_94214: f) assuming the nature and intended purpose of the business relationship where this is obvious, for example in the case of certain gift cards that do not fall under the closed loop/closed network exemption;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:70]
PARAGRAPH_94216: g) reducing the intensity of monitoring as long as a certain monetary threshold is not reached. As ongoing monitoring is an important means of obtaining more information on customer risk factors (see above) during the course of a customer relationship, that threshold for both individual transactions and transactions that appear to be linked over the course of 12 months should be set at a level that the firm has assessed as presenting a low risk for both terrorist financing and money laundering purposes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94218: Guideline 11: Sectoral guideline for money remitters

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94219: 11.1. Money remitters are payment institutions or e-money institutions or credit institutions that have been authorised in line with Directive (EU) 2015/2366 to provide and execute payment services throughout the EU. The businesses in this sector are diverse and range from individual businesses to complex chain operators.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94220: 11.2. Many money remitters use agents to provide payment services on their behalf. Agents often provide payment services as an ancillary component to their main business and they may not themselves be obliged entities under applicable AML/CFT legislation; accordingly, their AML/CFT expertise may be limited.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94221: 11.3. The nature of the service provided can expose money remitters to ML/TF risk. This is due to the simplicity and speed of transactions, their worldwide reach and their often cash- based character. Furthermore, the nature of this payment service means that money remitters often carry out occasional transactions rather than establishing a business relationship with their customers, which means that their understanding of the ML/TF risk associated with the customer may be limited.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94222: 11.4. Money remitters should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. Firms whose authorisation includes the provision of business activities as Payment Initiation Services and Account Initiation Services should also refer to the sectoral guideline 18.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94223: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94224: Product, service and transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94225: 11.5. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94226: a) the product allows high-value or unlimited-value transactions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94227: b) the product or service has a global reach;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94228: c) the transaction is cash-based or funded with anonymous electronic money, including electronic money benefiting from the exemption under Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94229: d) transfers are made from one or more payers in different countries to a local payee.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94230: 11.6. The following factor may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:71]
PARAGRAPH_94231: a) the funds used in the transfer come from an account held in the payer's name at an EEA credit or financial institution

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94233: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94234: 11.7. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94235: a) The customer's business activity:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94236: i. The customer owns or operates a business that handles large amounts of cash.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94237: i. The customer's business has a complicated ownership structure.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94238: iii. The customer's activity could be associated with TF because he is publicly known to have extremism sympathies or are known to be linked to an organised crime group.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94239: b) The customer's behaviour:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94240: i. The customer's needs may be better serviced elsewhere, for example because the money remitter is not local to the customer or the customer's business.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94241: ii. The customer appears to be acting for someone else, for example others watch over the customer or are visible outside the place where the transaction is made, or the customer reads instructions from a note.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94242: iii. The customer's behaviour makes no apparent economic sense, for example the customer accepts a poor exchange rate or high charges unquestioningly, requests a transaction in a currency that is not official tender or commonly used in the jurisdiction where the customer and/or recipient is located or requests or provides large amounts of currency in either low or high denominations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94243: iv. The customer's transactions are always just below applicable thresholds, including the CDD threshold for occasional transactions in Article 11(b) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 and the EUR 1 000 threshold specified in Article 5(2) of Regulation (EU) 2015/847.16 Firms should note that the threshold in Article 5(2) of Regulation (EU) 2015/847 applies only to transactions that are not funded by cash or anonymous electronic money.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94244: V. The customer's use of the service is unusual, for example they send or receive money to or from themselves or send funds on immediately after receiving them.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94245: vi. The customer appears to know little or is reluctant to provide information about the payee.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:72]
PARAGRAPH_94246: 16 Regulation (EU) 2015/847 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 20 May 2015 on information accompanying transfers of funds and repealing Regulation (EC) No 1781/2006.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94248: vii. Several of the firm's customers transfer funds to the same payee or appear to have the same identification information, for example address or telephone number.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94249: viii. An incoming transaction is not accompanied by the required information on the payer or payee.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94250: ix. The amount sent or received is at odds with the customer's income (if known).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94251: x. The increase of volume or number of transactions is not related to a usual pattern like salary remittance or cultural celebration.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94252: xi. The customer provides inconsistent biographical data or identification documents containing inconsistent information.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94253: 11.8. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94254: a) The customer is a long-standing customer of the firm whose past behaviour has not given rise to suspicion and there are no indications that the ML/TF risk might be increased

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94255: b) The amount transferred is low; however, firms should note that low amounts alone will not be enough to discount TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94256: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94257: 11.9. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94258: a) There are no restrictions on the funding instrument, for example in the case of cash or payments from E-money products that benefit from the exemption in Article 12 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, wire transfers or cheques.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94259: b) The distribution channel used provides a degree of anonymity.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94260: c) The service is provided entirely online without adequate safeguards.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94261: d) The money remittance service is provided through agents that:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94262: i. represent more than one principal;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:73]
PARAGRAPH_94263: ii. have unusual turnover patterns compared with other agents in similar locations, for example unusually high or low transaction sizes, unusually large cash transactions or a high number of transactions that fall just under the CDD threshold, or undertake business outside normal business hours;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94265: iii. undertake a large proportion of business with payers or payees from jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94266: iv. appear to be unsure about, or inconsistent in, the application of group-wide AML/CFT policies; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94267: V. are not from the financial sector and conduct another business as their main business.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94268: e) The money remittance service is provided through a large network of agents in different jurisdictions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94269: f) The money remittance service is provided through an overly complex payment chain, for example with a large number of intermediaries operating in different jurisdictions or allowing for untraceable (formal and informal) settlement systems.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94270: 11.10.The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94271: a) Agents are themselves regulated financial institutions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94272: b) The service can be funded only by transfers from an account held in the customer's name at an EEA credit or financial institution or an account over which the customer can be shown to have control.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94273: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94274: 11.11.The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94275: a) The payer or the payee is located , or the transaction is executed from an IP address, in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions known to provide funding or support for terrorist activities or where groups committing terrorist offences are known to be operating, and jurisdictions subject to financial sanctions, embargoes or measures that are related to terrorism, financing of terrorism or proliferation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94276: b) The payee is resident in a jurisdiction that has no, or a less developed, formal banking sector, which means that informal money remittance services, such as hawala, may be used at point of payment.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94277: c) The firm's counterparty is located in a third country [associated with higher ML/TF risk]

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:74]
PARAGRAPH_94278: d) The payer or the payee is located in a high-risk third country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94281: 11.12.Since many money remitters' business is primarily transaction-based, firms should consider which monitoring systems and controls they put in place to ensure that they detect money-laundering and terrorist financing attempts even where the CDD information they hold on the customer is basic or missing because no business relationship has been established. When analysing appropriate monitoring systems, money remitters should ensure that are aligned with the size and complexity of the business and their transaction volume.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94282: 11.13. Firms should in any case put in place:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94283: a) systems to identify linked transactions, including those that might amount to a business relationship according to their policies and procedures, such as systems to identify series of transactions bellow EUR 1 000 which have the same payer and payee and an element of duration;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94284: b) systems to identify whether transactions from different customers are destined for the same payee;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94285: c) systems to permit as far as possible the establishment of the source of funds and the destination of funds;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94286: d) systems that allow the full traceability of both transactions and the number of operators included in the payment chain;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94287: e) systems that identify whether a transfer is made to, or received from, a high risk third country; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94288: f) systems to ensure that throughout the payment chain only those duly authorised to provide money remittance services can intervene.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94289: 11.14. Where the risk associated with an occasional transaction or business relationship is increased, firms should apply EDD in line with Title I, including, where appropriate, increased transaction monitoring (e.g. increased frequency or lower thresholds). Conversely, where the risk associated with an occasional transaction or business relationship is low and to the extent permitted by national legislation, firms may be able to apply SDD measures in line with Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94290: 11.15.To comply with Article 18a of Directive (EU) 2015/849 in respect of relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, money remitter should apply the EDD measures set out in this regard in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:75]
PARAGRAPH_94291: Use of agents

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:76] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94293: 11.16.Money remitters using agents to provide payment services should know who their agents as set out in Article 19 of Directive (EU) 2015/2366 are. As part of this, money remitters should establish and maintain appropriate and risk- sensitive policies and procedures to counter the risk that their agents may engage in, or be used for, ML/TF, including by:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:76]
PARAGRAPH_94294: a) Identifying the person who owns or controls the agent where the agent is a legal person, to be satisfied that the ML/TF risk to which the money remitter is exposed as a result of its use of the agent is not increased.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:76]
PARAGRAPH_94295: b) Obtaining evidence, in line with the requirements of Article 19(1)(c) of Directive (EU) 2015/2366, that the directors and other persons responsible for the management of the agent are fit and proper persons, including by considering their honesty, integrity and reputation. Any enquiry the money remitter makes should be proportionate to the nature, complexity and scale of the ML/TF risk inherent in the payment services provided by the agent and could be based on the money remitter's CDD procedures.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:76] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94296: c) Taking reasonable measures to satisfy themselves that the agent's AML/CFT internal controls are appropriate and remain appropriate throughout the agency relationship, for example by monitoring a sample of the agent's transactions or reviewing the agent's controls on site. Where an agent's internal AML/CFT controls differ from the money remitter's, for example because the agent represents more than one principal or because the agent is itself an obliged entity under applicable AML/CFT legislation, the money remitter should assess and manage the risk that these differences might affect its own, and the agent's, AML/CFT compliance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:76] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94297: d) Providing AML/CFT training to agents to ensure that agents have an adequate understanding of relevant ML/TF risks and the quality of the AML/CFT controls the money remitter expects.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94299: Guideline 12: Sectoral guideline for wealth management

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94300: 12.1. Wealth management is the provision of banking and other financial services to high-net- worth individuals and their families or businesses. It is also known as private banking. Clients of wealth management firms can expect dedicated relationship management staff to provide tailored services covering, for example, banking (e.g. current accounts, mortgages and foreign exchange), investment management and advice, fiduciary services, safe custody, insurance, family office services, tax and estate planning and associated facilities, including legal support.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94301: 12.2. Many of the features typically associated with wealth management, such as wealthy and influential clients; very high-value transactions and portfolios; complex products and services, including tailored investment products; and an expectation of confidentiality and discretion are indicative of a higher risk for money laundering relative to those typically present in retail banking. Wealth management firms' services may be particularly vulnerable to abuse by clients who wish to conceal the origins of their funds or, for example, evade tax in their home jurisdiction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94302: 12.3. Firms in this sector should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. The sectoral guidelines 9, 14 and 17 in Title I, may also be relevant in this context.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94303: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94304: Product, service and transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94305: 12.4. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94306: a) customers requesting large amounts of cash or other physical stores of value such as precious metals;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94307: b) very high-value transactions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
