PARAGRAPH_94308: c) financial arrangements involving jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk (firms should pay particular attention to countries that have a culture of banking secrecy or that do not comply with international tax transparency standards);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:77]
PARAGRAPH_94309: d) lending (including mortgages) secured against the value of assets in other jurisdictions, particularly countries where it is difficult to ascertain whether the customer has legitimate title to the collateral, or where the identities of parties guaranteeing the loan are hard to verify;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94311: e) the use of complex business structures such as trusts and private investment vehicles, particularly where the identity of the ultimate beneficial owner may be unclear;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94312: f) business taking place across multiple countries, particularly where it involves multiple providers of financial services;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94313: g) cross-border arrangements where assets are deposited or managed in another financial institution, either of the same financial group or outside the group, particularly where the other financial institution is based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions with higher levels of predicate offences, a weak AML/CFT regime or weak tax transparency standards.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94314: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94315: 12.5. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94316: a) Customers with income and/or wealth from high-risk sectors such as arms, the extractive industries, construction, gambling or private military contractors.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94317: b) Customers about whom credible allegations of wrongdoing have been made.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94318: c) Customers who expect unusually high levels of confidentiality or discretion.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94319: d) Customers whose spending or transactional behaviour makes it difficult to establish 'normal', or expected patterns of behaviour.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94320: e) Very wealthy and influential clients, including customers with a high public profile, non-resident customers and PEPs. Where a customer or a customer's beneficial owner is a PEP, firms must always apply EDD in line with Articles 18 to 22 of Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94321: f) The customer requests that the firm facilitates the customer being provided with a product or service by a third party without a clear business or economic rationale.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94322: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78]
PARAGRAPH_94323: 12.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:78] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94324: a) Business is conducted in countries that have a culture of banking secrecy or do not comply with international tax transparency standards.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94326: b) The customer lives in, or their funds derive from activity in, a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94328: 12.7. The staff member managing a wealth management firm's relationship with a customer (the relationship manager) typically plays a key role in assessing risk. The relationship manager's close contact with the customer will facilitate the collection of information that allows a fuller picture of the purpose and nature of the customer's business to be formed (e.g. an understanding of the client's source of wealth, the destination of funds, why complex or unusual arrangements may nonetheless be genuine and legitimate, or why extra security may be appropriate). This close contact may, however, also lead to conflicts of interest if the relationship manager becomes too close to the customer, to the detriment of the firm's efforts to manage the risk of financial crime. Consequently, independent oversight of risk assessment will also be appropriate, provided by, for example, the compliance department and senior management.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94329: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94330: 12.8. To comply with Article 18a in respect of relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, firms should apply the EDD measures set out in this regard in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94331: a) Obtaining and verifying more information about clients than in standard risk situations and reviewing and updating this information both on a regular basis and when prompted by material changes to a client's profile. Firms should perform reviews on a risk-sensitive basis, reviewing higher risk clients at least annually but more frequently if risk dictates. These procedures may include those for recording any visits to clients' premises, whether at their home or business, including any changes to client profile or other information that may affect risk assessment that these visits prompt.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94332: b) Establishing the source of wealth and funds; where the risk is particularly high and/or where the firm has doubts about the legitimate origin of the funds, verifying the source of wealth and funds may be the only adequate risk mitigation tool. The source of funds or wealth can be verified, by reference to, inter alia:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94333: i. an original or certified copy of a recent pay slip;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94334: ii. written confirmation of annual salary signed by an employer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:79]
PARAGRAPH_94335: iii. an original or certified copy of contract of sale of, for example, investments or a company;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94337: iv. written confirmation of sale signed by a lawyer or solicitor;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94338: v. an original or certified copy of a will or grant of probate;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94339: vi. written confirmation of inheritance signed by a lawyer, solicitor, trustee or executor;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94340: vii. an internet search of a company registry to confirm the sale of a company;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94341: viii. Performing greater levels of scrutiny and due diligence on business relationships than would be typical in mainstream financial service provision, such as in retail banking or investment management.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:80]
PARAGRAPH_94342: c) Establishing the destination of funds.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94344: Guideline 13: Sectoral guideline for trade finance providers

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94345: 13.1. Trade finance means managing a payment to facilitate the movement of goods (and the provision of services) either domestically or across borders. When goods are shipped internationally, the importer faces the risk that the goods will not arrive; while the exporter may be concerned, that payment will not be forthcoming. To lessen these dangers, many trade finance instruments therefore place banks in the middle of the transaction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94346: 13.2. Trade finance can take many different forms. These include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94347: a) 'Open account' transactions: these are transactions where the buyer makes a payment once they have received the goods. These are the most common means of financing trade, but the underlying trade-related nature of the transaction will often not be known to the banks executing the fund transfer. Banks should refer to the guidance in Title I to manage the risk associated with such transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94348: b) Documentary letters of credit (LCs) that have many variations and are suited to a different situation respectively: an LC is a financial instrument issued by a bank that guarantees payment to a named beneficiary (typically an exporter) upon presentation of certain 'complying' documents specified in the credit terms (e.g. evidence that goods have been dispatched).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94349: c) Documentary bills for collection (BCs): a BC refers to a process by which payment, or an accepted draft, is collected by a 'collecting' bank from an importer of goods for onward payment to the exporter. The collecting bank gives the relevant trade documentation (which will have been received from the exporter, normally through their bank) to the importer in return.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94350: 13.3. Other trade finance products such as forfaiting or structured financing, or wider activity such as project finance, are outside the scope of these sectoral guidelines. Banks offering these products should refer to the general guidance in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81]
PARAGRAPH_94351: 13.4. Trade finance products can be abused for money laundering and terrorist financing purposes. For example, the buyer and seller may collude to misrepresent the price, type, quality or quantity of goods in order to transfer funds or value between countries.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:81] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94352: 13.5. Banks should take into account that the International Chamber of Commerce (ICC) has developed standards such as the Uniform Customs & Practice for Documentary Credits (600) that is a set of rules which apply to finance institutions which issue Letters of Credit that govern the use of LCs and BCs, but that these do not cover matters related to financial crime. Banks should note that these standards do not have legal force and their use does not mean that banks do not need to comply with their legal and regulatory AML/CFT obligations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94354: 13.6. Firms in this sector should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. The sectoral guideline 8 in Title II may also be relevant in this context.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94355: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94356: 13.7. Banks that are party to trade finance transactions often have access only to partial information about the transaction and the parties to it. Trade documentation can be diverse, and banks may not have expert knowledge of the different types of trade documentation they receive. This can make the identification and assessment of ML/TF risk challenging.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94357: 13.8. Banks should, nevertheless, use common sense and professional judgement to assess the extent to which the information and documentation they have could give rise to concern or suspicion of ML/TF.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94358: 13.9. To the extent possible, banks should consider the following risk factors:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94359: Transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94360: 13.10. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94361: a) The transaction is unusually large given what is known about a customer's previous line of business and trading activity.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94362: b) The transaction is highly structured, fragmented or complex, involving multiple parties, without apparent legitimate justification

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94363: c) Copy documents are used in situations where original documentation would be expected, without reasonable explanation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94364: d) There are significant discrepancies in documentation, for example between the description of the type, quantity or quality of goods in key documents (i.e. invoices, insurance and transport documents) and actual goods shipped, to the extent that this is known.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94365: e) The type, quantity and value of goods is inconsistent with the bank's knowledge of the buyer's business.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94366: f) The goods transacted are higher risk for money-laundering purposes, for example certain commodities the prices of which can fluctuate significantly, which can make bogus prices difficult to detect.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:82]
PARAGRAPH_94367: g) The agreed value of goods or shipment is over- or under-insured or multiple insurances are used, to the extent this is known.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94369: h) The goods transacted require export licenses, such as specific export authorizations for dual-use items that are goods, software and technology that can be used for both civilian and military applications.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94370: i) The trade documentation does not comply with applicable laws or standards.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94371: j) Unit pricing appears unusual, based on what the bank knows about the goods and trade.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94372: k) The transaction is otherwise unusual, for example LCs are frequently amended without a clear rationale or goods are shipped through another jurisdiction for no apparent commercial reason.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94373: I) The goods traded are destined to a party or country that is subject to a sanction, an embargo or a similar measure issued by, for example, the Union or the United Nations, or in support of such party or country.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94374: 13.11. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94375: a) Independent inspection agents have verified the quality and quantity of the goods and the presence of the necessary documents and authorisations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94376: b) Transactions involve established counterparties that have a proven track record of transacting with each other and due diligence has previously been carried out.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94377: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94378: 13.12. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94379: a) The transaction and/or the parties involved are out of line with what the bank knows about the customer's previous activity or line of business (e.g. the goods being shipped, or the shipping volumes, are inconsistent with what is known about the importer or exporter's business).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94380: b) There are indications that the buyer and seller may be colluding, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94381: i. the buyer and seller are controlled by the same person;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94382: ii. transacting businesses have the same address, provide only a registered agent's address, or have other address inconsistencies;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94383: iii. the buyer is willing or keen to accept or waive discrepancies in the documentation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:83]
PARAGRAPH_94384: c) The customer is unable or reluctant to provide relevant documentation to support the transaction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94386: d) The customer faces difficulties explaining the rationale of the entire export process or is unable to explain the content and meaning of the underlying to the LC or BC documents.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94387: e) The buyer's legal structure does not allow the identification of its owners or it uses agents or third parties to represent the buyers rights and interests.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94388: 13.13.The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94389: a) The customer is an existing customer whose business is well known to the bank and the transaction is in line with that business.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94390: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94391: 13.14. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94392: a) A country associated with the transaction (including the country from which the goods originated, for which they are destined or transited through, or where either party to the transaction is based) has no currency exchange controls in place. This increases the risk that the transaction's true purpose is to export currency in contravention of local law.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94393: b) A country associated with the transaction has higher levels of predicate offences (e.g. those related to the narcotics trade, smuggling or counterfeiting) or free trade zones.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94394: c) Transaction is executed under auspices of governmental or international organizations or foundations to support the victims of natural disaster or persons affected from war conflict or civil unrest.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94395: 13.15. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94396: a) The trade is within the EU/EEA.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84]
PARAGRAPH_94397: b) Countries associated with the transaction have an AML/CFT regime not less robust than that required under Directive (EU) 2015/849 and are associated with low levels of predicate offences.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:84] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94399: 13.16.Banks must carry out CDD on the instructing party. In practice, most banks will only accept instructions from existing customers and the wider business relationship that the bank has with the customer may assist its due diligence efforts.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94401: 13.17.Where a bank provides trade finance services to a customer, it should take steps, as part of its CDD process, to understand its customer's business . Examples of the type of information the bank could obtain include the countries with which the customer trades, the trading routes used, goods traded, who the customer does business with (buyers, suppliers, etc.), whether the customer uses agents or third parties, and, if so, where these are based. This should help banks understand who the customer is and aid the detection of unusual or suspicious transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94402: 13.18.Where a bank is a correspondent, it must apply CDD measures to the respondent. Correspondent banks should follow the sectoral guideline 8 on correspondent banking.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94403: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94404: 13.19.To comply with Article 18a in respect of relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, firms should apply the EDD measures set out in this regard in Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94405: 13.20.In other higher risk situations, banks must also apply EDD. As part of this, banks should consider whether performing more thorough due diligence checks on the transaction itself and on other parties to the transaction (including non-customers) would be appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94406: 13.21.Checks on other parties to the transaction may include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94407: a) Taking steps to better understand the ownership or background of other parties to the transaction, in particular where they are based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk or where they handle high-risk goods. This may include checks of company registries and third party intelligence sources, and open source internet searches.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94408: b) Obtaining more information on the financial situation of the parties involved.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94409: 13.22.Checks on transactions may include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94410: a) using third party or open source data sources, for example the International Maritime Bureau (for warning notices, bills of lading, shipping and pricing checks) or shipping lines' free container tracking service to verify the information provided and to check that the purpose of the transaction is legitimate;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94411: b) using professional judgement to consider whether the pricing of goods makes commercial sense, in particular in relation to traded commodities for which reliable and up-to-date pricing information can be obtained;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:85]
PARAGRAPH_94412: c) checking that the weights and volumes of goods being shipped are consistent with the shipping method.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:86] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94414: 13.23.Since LCs and BCs are largely paper-based and accompanied by trade-related documents (e.g. invoices, bills of lading and manifests), automated transaction monitoring may not be feasible. The processing bank should assess these documents for consistency with the terms of the trade transaction and require staff to use professional expertise and judgement to consider whether any unusual features warrant the application of EDD measures or give rise to suspicion of ML/TF.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:86]
PARAGRAPH_94415: Simplified customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:86]
PARAGRAPH_94416: 13.24. The checks banks routinely carry out to detect fraud and ensure the transaction conforms to the standards set by the International Chamber of Commerce mean that, in practice, they will not apply SDD measures even in lower risk situations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94418: Guideline 14: Sectoral guideline for life insurance undertakings

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94419: 14.1. Life insurance products are designed to financially protect the policy holder against the risk of an uncertain future event, such as death, illness or outliving savings in retirement (longevity risk). Protection is achieved by an insurer who pools the financial risks that many different policy holders are faced with. Life insurance products can also be bought as investment products or for pension purposes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94420: 14.2. Life insurance products are provided through different distribution channels to customers who may be natural or legal persons or legal arrangements. The beneficiary of the contract may be the policy holder or a nominated or designated third party; the beneficiary may also change during the term and the original beneficiary may never benefit.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94421: 14.3. Most life insurance products are designed for the long term and some will only pay out on a verifiable event, such as death or retirement. This means that many life insurance products are not sufficiently flexible to be the first vehicle of choice for money launderers. However, as with other financial services products, there is a risk that the funds used to purchase life insurance may be the proceeds of crime.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94422: 14.4. Firms in this sector should consider the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. The sectoral guidelines 12 and 16 in Title II may also be relevant in this context. Where intermediaries are used, the delivery channel risk factors set out in Title I will be relevant.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94423: 14.5. Intermediaries may also find these guidelines useful.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94424: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94425: Product, service and transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94426: 14.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94427: a) Flexibility of payments, for example the product allows:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94428: i. payments from unidentified third parties;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94429: ii. high-value or unlimited-value premium payments, overpayments or large volumes of lower value premium payments;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94430: iii. cash payments.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94431: b) Ease of access to accumulated funds, for example the product allows partial withdrawals or early surrender at any time, with limited charges or fees.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:87]
PARAGRAPH_94432: c) Negotiability, for example the product can be:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94434: i. traded on a secondary market;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94435: ii. used as collateral for a loan.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94436: d) Anonymity, for example the product facilitates or allows the anonymity of the customer.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94437: 14.7. Factors that may contribute to reducing risk include: The product:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94438: a) only pays out against a pre-defined event, for example death, or on a specific date, such as in the case of credit life insurance policies covering consumer and mortgage loans, which only pay out on the death of the insured person;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94439: b) has no surrender value;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94440: c) has no investment element;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94441: d) has no third party payment facility;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94442: e) requires that total investment is curtailed at a low value;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94443: f) is a life insurance policy where the premium is low;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94444: g) only allows small-value regular premium payments, for example no overpayment;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94445: h) is accessible only through employers, for example a pension, superannuation or similar scheme that provides retirement benefits to employees, where contributions are made by way of deduction from wages and the scheme rules do not permit the assignment of a member's interest under the scheme;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94446: i) cannot be redeemed in the short or medium term, as in the case of pension schemes without an early surrender option;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94447: j) cannot be used as collateral;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94448: k) does not allow cash payments;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94449: I) has conditions limiting the availability of funds that must be met to benefit from tax relief.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94450: Customer and beneficiary risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94451: 14.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:88]
PARAGRAPH_94452: a) The nature of the customer, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94454: i. legal persons whose structure makes it difficult to identify the beneficial owner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94455: ii. the customer or the beneficial owner of the customer is a PEP;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94456: iii. the beneficiary of the policy or the beneficial owner of this beneficiary is a PEP;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94457: iv. the customer's age is unusual for the type of product sought (e.g. the customer is very young or very old);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94458: V. the contract does not match the customer's wealth situation;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94459: vi. the customer's profession or activities are regarded as particularly likely to be related to money laundering, for example because they are known to be very cash intensive or exposed to a high risk of corruption;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94460: vii. the contract is subscribed by a 'gatekeeper', such as a fiduciary company, acting on behalf of the customer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94461: viii. the policy holder and/or the beneficiary of the contract are companies with nominee shareholders and/or shares in bearer form.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94462: b) The customer's behaviour:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94463: i. In relation to the contract, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94464: a. the customer frequently transfers the contract to another insurer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94465: b. frequent and unexplained surrenders, especially when the refund is done to different bank accounts;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94466: c. the customer makes frequent or unexpected use of 'free look' provisions/'cooling-off' periods in particular where the refund is made to an apparently unrelated third party;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94467: d. the customer incurs a high cost by seeking early termination of a product;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94468: e. the customer transfers the contract to an apparently unrelated third party;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:89]
PARAGRAPH_94469: f. the customer's request to change or increase the sum insured and/or the premium payment are unusual or excessive.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94471: ii. In relation to the beneficiary, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94472: a. the insurer is made aware of a change in beneficiary only when the claim is made;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94473: b. the customer changes the beneficiary clause and nominates an apparently unrelated third party;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94474: c. the insurer, the customer, the beneficial owner, the beneficiary or the beneficial owner of the beneficiary are in different jurisdictions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94475: iii. In relation to payments, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94476: a. the customer uses unusual payment methods, such as cash or structured monetary instruments or other forms of payment vehicles fostering anonymity;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94477: b. payments from different bank accounts without explanation;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94478: c. payments from banks that are not established in the customer's country of residence;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94479: d. the customer makes frequent or high-value overpayments where this was not expected;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94480: e. payments received from unrelated third parties;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94481: f. catch-up contribution to a retirement plan close to retirement date.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94482: 14.9. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk. In the case of corporate-owned life insurance, the customer is:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94483: a) a credit or financial institution that is subject to requirements to combat money laundering and the financing of terrorism and supervised for compliance with these requirements in a manner that is consistent with Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94484: b) a public administration or a public enterprise from an EEA jurisdiction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94485: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:90]
PARAGRAPH_94486: 14.10. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94488: a) non-face-to-face sales, such as online, postal or telephone sales, without adequate safeguards, such as electronic signatures or electronic identification means that comply with Regulation (EU) No 910/2014;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94489: b) long chains of intermediaries;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94490: c) an intermediary is used in unusual circumstances (e.g. unexplained geographical distance).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94491: 14.11.The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94492: a) Intermediaries are well known to the insurer, who is satisfied that the intermediary applies CDD measures commensurate to the risk associated with the relationship and in line with those required under Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94493: b) The product is only available to employees of certain companies that have a contract with the insurer to provide life insurance for their employees, for example as part of a benefits package.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94494: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94495: 14.12. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94496: a) The insurer, the customer, the beneficial owner, the beneficiary or the beneficial owner of the beneficiary are based in, or associated with, jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions without effective AML/CFT supervision.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94497: b) Premiums are paid through accounts held with financial institutions established in jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions without effective AML/CFT supervision.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94498: c) The intermediary is based in, or associated with, jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk. Firms should pay particular attention to jurisdictions without effective AML/CFT supervision.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94499: 14.13. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94500: a) Countries are identified by credible sources, such as mutual evaluations or detailed assessment reports, as having effective AML/CFT systems.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:91]
PARAGRAPH_94501: b) Countries are identified by credible sources as having a low level of corruption and other criminal activity.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94504: 14.14.Article 13(5) of Directive (EU) 2015/849 provides that, for life insurance business, firms must apply CDD measures not only to the customer and beneficial owner but also to the beneficiaries as soon as they are identified or designated. This means that firms must:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92]
PARAGRAPH_94505: a) obtain the name of the beneficiary where either a natural or legal person or an arrangement is identified as the beneficiary; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92]
PARAGRAPH_94506: b) obtain sufficient information to be satisfied that the identities of the beneficiaries can be established at the time of payout where the beneficiaries are a class of persons or designated by certain characteristics. For example, where the beneficiary is 'my future grandchildren', the insurer could obtain information about the policy holder's children.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94507: 14.15.Firms must verify the beneficiaries' identities at the latest at the time of payout.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94508: 14.16. Where the firm knows that the life insurance has been assigned to a third party, who will receive the value of the policy, they must identify the beneficial owner at the time of the assignment.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94509: 14.17.In order to comply with Article 13(6) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, when the beneficiaries of trusts or of similar legal arrangements are a class of persons or designated by certain characteristics, firms should obtain sufficient information to be satisfied that the identities of the beneficiaries can be established at the time of payout or at the time of the exercise by the beneficiaries of their vested rights.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92]
PARAGRAPH_94510: Enhanced customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94511: 14.18.To comply with Article 18a in respect of relationships or transactions involving high-risk third countries, firms should apply the EDD measures set out in this regard in Title I. The following EDD measures may be appropriate in all other high-risk situation:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:92] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94512: a) Where the customer makes use of the 'free look'/'cooling-off' period, the premium should be refunded to the customer's bank account from which the funds were paid. Firms should ensure that they have verified the customer's identity in line with Article 13 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 before making a refund, in particular where the premium is large or the circumstances appear otherwise unusual. Firms should also consider whether the cancellation gives rise to suspicion about the transaction and whether submitting a suspicious activity report would be appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94514: b) Additional steps may be taken to strengthen the firm's knowledge about the customer, the beneficial owner, the beneficiary or the beneficiary's beneficial owner, the third party payers and payees. Examples include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94515: i. not using the derogation in Article 14(2) of Directive (EU) 2015/849, which provides for an exemption from upfront CDD;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94516: ii. verifying the identity of other relevant parties, including third party payers and payees, before the beginning of the business relationship;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94517: iii. obtaining additional information to establish the intended nature of the business relationship;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94518: iv. obtaining additional information on the customer and updating more regularly the identification data of the customer and beneficial owner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94519: V. if the payer is different from the customer, establishing the reason why;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94520: vi. verifying identities on the basis of more than one reliable and independent source;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94521: vii. establishing the customer's source of wealth and source of funds, for example employment and salary details, inheritance or divorce settlements;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94522: viii. where possible, identifying the beneficiary and verifying their identity at the beginning of the business relationship, rather than waiting until they are identified or designated, bearing in mind that the beneficiary can change over the term of the policy;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94523: ix. identifying and verifying the identity of the beneficiary's beneficial owner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94524: x. in line with Articles 20 and 21 of Directive (EU) 2015/849, taking measures to determine whether the customer is a PEP and taking reasonable measures to determine whether the beneficiary or the beneficiary's beneficial owner is a PEP at the time of assignment, in whole or in part, of the policy or, at the latest, at the time of payout;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93]
PARAGRAPH_94525: xi. requiring the first payment to be carried out through an account in the customer's name with a bank subject to CDD standards that are not less robust than those required under Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:93] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94526: 14.19.Article 20 of Directive (EU) 2015/849 requires that, where the risk associated with a PEP relationship is high, firms must not only apply CDD measures in line with Article 13 of the Directive but also inform senior management before the payout of the policy so that senior management can take an informed view of the ML/TF risk associated with the situation and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94528: decide on the most appropriate measures to mitigate that risk; in addition, firms must conduct EDD on the entire business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94529: 14.20.Firms should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94530: a) obtain additional information on the business relationship so as to be able to understand the nature of the relationship between the customer/the insured and the beneficiary, and of the relationship between the payer and the beneficiary if the payer is different from the customer/the insured; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94531: b) enhance their scrutiny on the source of funds.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94532: 14.21. Where the beneficiary is a PEP and is expressly named, firms should not wait until the payout of the policy to conduct the enhanced scrutiny of the entire business relationship.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94533: 14.22.More frequent and more in-depth monitoring of transactions may be required (including where necessary, establishing the source of funds).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94534: Simplified customer due diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94535: 14.23. The following measures may satisfy some of the CDD requirements in low-risk situations (to the extent permitted by national legislation):

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94536: a) Firms may be able to assume that the verification of the identity of the customer is fulfilled on the basis of a payment drawn on an account that the firm is satisfied is in the sole or joint name of the customer with an EEA- regulated credit institution.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:94]
PARAGRAPH_94537: b) Firms may be able to assume that the verification of the identity of the beneficiary of the contract is fulfilled on the basis of a payment made to an account in the beneficiary's name at a regulated EEA credit institution.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94539: Guideline 15: Sectoral guideline for investment firms

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94540: 15.1. Investment firms as defined in point (1) of Article 4(1) of Directive 2014/65/EUshould consider when providing or executing investment services or activities as defined in point (2) of Article 4(1) of Directive (EU) 2014/65 the following risk factors and measures alongside those set out in Title I of these guidelines. The sectoral guideline 12 may also be relevant in this context.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94541: 15.2. To comply with their obligations under Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms in this sector should consider that:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94542: a) ML/TF risk in this sector is driven primarily by the risk associated with the clients whom investment firms serve; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94543: b) the nature of the activities which investment firms undertake means that they may be exposed to predicate offences such as market abuse, which may lead to ML/TF.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94544: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94545: Product, service or transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94546: 15.3. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94547: a) transactions are unusually large, in the context of the customer's profile;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94548: b) settlement arrangements that are non-standard or appear irregular;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94549: c) mirror trades or transactions involving securities used for currency conversion that appear unusual or have no apparent business or economic purposes;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94550: d) the product or service is structured in a way that may present difficulties in identifying the customers; third party payments are possible.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94551: 15.4. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94552: a) The product or service is subject to mandatory transparency and/or disclosure requirements.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94553: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94554: 15.5. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94555: a) The customer's behaviour, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:95]
PARAGRAPH_94556: i. the rationale for the investment lacks an obvious economic purpose;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94558: ii. the customer asks to repurchase or redeem a long-term investment within a short period after the initial investment or before the payout date without a clear rationale, in particular where this results in financial loss or payment of high transaction fees;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94559: iii. the customer requests the repeated purchase and sale of shares within a short period of time without an obvious strategy or economic rationale

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94560: iv. unwillingness to provide CDD information on the customer and the beneficial owner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94561: V. frequent changes to CDD information or payment details;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94562: vi. the customer transfers funds in excess of those required for the investment and asks for surplus amounts to be reimbursed;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94563: vii. the circumstances in which the customer makes use of the 'cooling-off' period give rise to suspicion;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94564: viii. using multiple accounts without previous notification, especially when these accounts are held in multiple or high-risk jurisdictions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94565: ix. the customer wishes to structure the relationship in such a way that multiple parties, for example nominee companies, are used in different jurisdictions, particularly where these jurisdictions are associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94566: b) The customer's nature, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94567: i. the customer is a company, a trust or other legal arrangements having a structure or functions similar to trusts, established in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk (firms should pay particular attention to those jurisdictions that do not comply effectively with international tax and information sharing transparency standards);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94568: ii. the customer is an investment vehicle that carries out little or no due diligence on its own clients;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94569: iii. the customer is an unregulated third party investment vehicle;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94570: iv. the customer's ownership and control structure is opaque;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94571: V. the customer or the beneficial owner is a PEP or holds another prominent position that might enable them to abuse their position for private gain;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:96]
PARAGRAPH_94572: vi. the customer is a non-regulated nominee company with unknown shareholders.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94574: c) The customer's business, for example the customer's funds are derived from business in sectors that are associated with a higher risk of financial crime, such as construction, pharmaceuticals and healthcare, the arms trade and defence, the extractive industries or public procurement.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94575: 15.6. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94576: a) The customer is an institutional investor whose status has been verified by an EEA government agency, for example a government-approved pensions scheme.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94577: b) The customer is a government body from an EEA jurisdiction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94578: c) The customer is a financial institution established in an EEA jurisdiction.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94579: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94580: 15.7. The following factors may contribute to increasing the risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94581: a) Complexity in the chain of reception and transmission of orders;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94582: b) Complexity in the distribution chain of investment products;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94583: c) The trading venue has members or participants located in high-risk jurisdictions

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94584: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94585: 15.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94586: a) The investor or their custodian is based in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94587: b) The funds come from a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94589: 15.9. When developing their AML/CFT policies and procedures to comply with their obligations under Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms in this sector should consider that depending on the type of activity they perform, they will be subject to rules under which they have to gather extensive information about their customers. Where this is the case, they should consider the extent to which information obtained for MiFID II and EMIR compliance purposes can be used also to meet their CDD obligations in standard situations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:97]
PARAGRAPH_94590: 15.10.In particular, investment managers typically need to develop a good understanding of their customers to help them identify suitable investment portfolios. The information gathered will be similar to that which firms obtain for AML/CFT purposes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:98]
PARAGRAPH_94592: 15.11.Firms should follow the EDD guidelines set out in Title I in higher risk situations. In addition, where the risk associated with a business relationship is high, firms should:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:98]
PARAGRAPH_94593: a) identify and, where necessary, verify the identity of the underlying investors of the firm's customer where the customer is an unregulated third party investment vehicle;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:98]
PARAGRAPH_94594: b) understand the reason for any payment or transfer to or from an unverified third party.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:98]
PARAGRAPH_94595: 15.12.To the extent permitted by national legislation, investment managers may apply the SDD guidelines set out in Title I in low-risk situations.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94597: Guideline 16: Sectoral guideline for providers of investment funds

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94598: 16.1. The provision of investment funds can involve multiple parties, such as the fund manager, appointed advisers, the depositary and sub-custodians, registrars and, in some cases, prime brokers. Similarly, the distribution of these funds can involve parties such as tied agents, advisory and discretionary wealth managers, platform service providers and independent financial advisers.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94599: 16.2. The type and number of parties involved in the fund's distribution process depends on the nature of the fund and may affect how much the fund knows about its customer and investors. The fund or, where the fund is not itself an obliged entity, the fund manager will retain responsibility for compliance with AML/CFT obligations, although aspects of the fund's CDD obligations may be carried out by one or more of these other parties subject to certain conditions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94600: 16.3. Investment funds may be used by persons or entities for ML/TF purposes:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94601: a) Retail funds are often distributed on a non-face-to-face basis; access to such funds is often easy and relatively quick to achieve, and holdings in such funds can be transferred between different parties.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94602: b) Alterative investment funds, such as hedge funds, real estate and private equity funds, tend to have a smaller number of investors, which can be private individuals as well as institutional investors (pension funds, funds of funds). Such funds that are designed for a limited number of high-net-worth individuals, or for family offices, can have an inherently higher risk of abuse for ML/TF purposes than retail funds, since investors are more likely to be in a position to exercise control over the fund assets. If investors exercise control over the assets, such funds are personal asset-holding vehicles, which are mentioned as a factor indicating potentially higher risk in Annex III to Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94603: c) Notwithstanding the often medium- to long-term nature of the investment, which can contribute to limiting the attractiveness of these products for money laundering purposes, they may still appeal to money launderers on the basis of their ability to generate growth and income.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94604: 16.4. This sectoral guideline is directed at:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94605: a) investment funds marketing their own shares or units, under Article 3(2)(d) of Directive (EU) 2015/849; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:99]
PARAGRAPH_94606: b) funds managers, where an investment fund is not incorporated.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94608: Other parties involved in the provision or distribution of the fund, for example intermediaries, may have to comply with their own CDD obligations and should refer to relevant chapters in these guidelines as appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94609: For funds and fund managers, the sectoral guidelines 8, 14 and 15 may also be relevant.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94610: Risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94611: Product, service or transaction risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94612: 16.5. The following factors may contribute to increasing the risk associated with the fund:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94613: a) The fund is designed for a limited number of individuals or family offices, for example a private fund or single investor fund.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94614: b) It is possible to subscribe to the fund and then quickly redeem the investment without the investor incurring significant administrative costs;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94615: c) Units of or shares in the fund can be treated without the fund or fund manager being notified at the time of the trade;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94616: d) Information about the investor is divided among several subjects.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94617: 16.6. The following factors may contribute to increasing the risk associated with the subscription:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94618: a) The subscription involves accounts or third parties in multiple jurisdictions, in particular where these jurisdictions are associated with a high ML/TF risk as defined in guideline 2.9 to 2.15 of Title I.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94619: b) The subscription involves third party subscribers or payees, in particular where this is unexpected.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94620: 16.7. The following factors may contribute to reducing the risk associated with the fund:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94621: a) Payments to and from third parties are not allowed.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94622: b) The fund is open to small-scale investors only, with investments capped.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94623: Customer risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94624: 16.8. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk. The customer's behaviour is unusual, for example:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:100]
PARAGRAPH_94625: a) The rationale for the investment lacks an obvious strategy or economic purpose or the customer makes investments that are inconsistent with the customer's overall financial situation, where this is known to the fund or fund manager.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94627: b) The customer requests the repeated purchase and/or sale of units or shares within a short period of time after the initial investment or before the payout date without a clear strategy or rationale, in particular where this results in financial loss or payment of high transaction fees.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94628: c) The customer transfers funds in excess of those required for the investment and asks for surplus amounts to be reimbursed.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94629: d) The customer uses multiple accounts without previous notification, especially when these accounts are held in multiple jurisdictions or jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94630: e) The customer wishes to structure the relationship in such a way that multiple parties, for example non-regulated nominee companies, are used in different jurisdictions, particularly where these jurisdictions are associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94631: f) The customer suddenly changes the settlement location without rationale, for example by changing the customer's country of residence.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94632: 16.9. The following factors may contribute to reducing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94633: a) the customer is an institutional investor whose status has been verified by an EEA government agency, for example a government-approved pensions scheme;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94634: b) the customer is a firm subject to AML/CFT requirements that are not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94635: Distribution channel risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94636: 16.10.The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94637: a) Complex distribution channels that limit the fund's oversight of its business relationships and restrict its ability to monitor transactions, for example the fund uses a large number of sub-distributors for distribution in third countries;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94638: b) the distributor is located in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk as defined in the general part of these guidelines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94639: 16.11. The following factors may indicate lower risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:101]
PARAGRAPH_94640: a) The fund admits only a designated type of low-risk investor, such as regulated firms investing as a principal (e.g. life companies) or corporate pension schemes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94642: b) The fund can be purchased and redeemed only through a firm subject to AML/CFT requirements that are not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94643: Country or geographical risk factors

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94644: 16.12. The following factors may contribute to increasing risk:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94645: a) The customers' or beneficial owners' funds have been generated in jurisdictions associated with higher ML/TF risk, in particular those associated with higher levels of predicate offences to money laundering.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94646: b) The customer requests their investment to be redeemed to an account in a credit institution located in a jurisdiction associated with higher ML/TF risk.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94648: 16.13. The measures funds or fund managers should take to comply with their CDD obligations will depend on how the customer or the investor (where the investor is not the customer) comes to the fund. The fund or fund manager should also take risk-sensitive measures to identify and verify the identity of the natural persons, if any, who ultimately own or control the customer (or on whose behalf the transaction is being conducted), for example by asking the prospective customer to declare, when they first apply to join the fund, whether they are investing on their own behalf or whether they are an intermediary investing on someone else's behalf.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94649: 16.14. The customer is:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94650: a) a natural or legal person who directly purchases units of or shares in a fund on their own account, and not on behalf of other, underlying investors; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94651: b) a firm that, as part of its economic activity, directly purchases units of or shares in its own name and exercises control over the investment for the ultimate benefit of one or more third parties who do not control the investment or investment decisions; or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94652: c) a firm, for example a financial intermediary, that acts in its own name and is registered in the fund's share/units register but acts on the account of, and pursuant to specific instructions from, one or more third parties (e.g. because the financial intermediary is a nominee, broker, multi-client pooled account/omnibus type account operator or operator of a similar passive-type arrangement); or

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:102]
PARAGRAPH_94653: d) a firm's customer, for example a financial intermediary's customer, where the firm is not registered in the fund's share/units register (e.g. because the

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94655: investment fund uses a financial intermediary to distribute fund shares or units, and the investor purchases units or shares through the firm and is registered in the fund's share/units register).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94656: Enhanced Customer Due Diligence

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94657: 16.15.In the situations described in guidelines 16.14 (a) and (b), examples of EDD measures a fund or fund manager should apply in high-risk situations include:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94658: a) obtaining additional customer information, such as the customer's reputation and background, before the establishment of the business relationship;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94659: b) taking additional steps to further verify the documents, data or information obtained;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94660: c) obtaining information on the source of funds and/or the source wealth of the customer and of the customer's beneficial owner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94661: d) requiring that the redemption payment is made through the initial account used for investment or an account in the sole or joint name of the customer;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94662: e) increasing the frequency and intensity of transaction monitoring;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94663: f) requireng that the first payment is made through a payment account held in the sole or joint name of the customer with an EEA-regulated credit or financial institution or a regulated credit or financial institution in a third country that has AML/CFT requirements that are not less robust than those required by Directive (EU) 2015/849;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94664: g) obtaining approval from senior management at the time the first transaction;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94665: h) enhanced monitoring of the customer relationship and individual transactions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_94666: 16.16.In the situations described in guideline 16.14 (c), where the risk is increased, in particular where the fund is designated for a limited number of investors, EDD measures must apply and may include those set out in guideline 16.15 above.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:103]
PARAGRAPH_94667: 16.17. Where a financial intermediary is based in a third country and has established a relationship similar to correspondent banking with the fund or the fund's manager, the measures described in guidelines 16.20 and 16.21 are not applicable. In such cases, to discharge their obligations under Article 19 of the Directive (EU) 2015/849, firms should apply toward the intermediary the enhanced due diligence measures listed in Sectoral Guideline 8. 14 to 8.17.
